## 1. Executive Summary

**D-RAP** (Dynamic Relay Access Point) is a self-built, open-source tunneling platform that exposes local development servers to the public internet through secure tunnels. Think **ngrok**, but built entirely from scratch вҖ” from raw TCP sockets, through custom protocol design, to a real-time dashboard.

**The one-liner:**

> Run a single CLI command. Get a public URL. Your localhost is now accessible from anywhere on Earth.

```
$ drap http 3000

D-RAP v1.0.0                                    
Status:     online                                
Account:    dev@axiom.io                          
Region:     us-east-1                             

Forwarding:  https://wild-fox-42.drap.io вҶ’ http://localhost:3000
             tcp://wild-fox-42.drap.io:44301 вҶ’ tcp://localhost:3000

Dashboard:   http://127.0.0.1:4040                
Requests:    0 total | 0/min                      

Connections: 1 active tunnel                      
```

**This is not a wrapper around SSH tunneling.** This is not a port-forward script. This is a full, ground-up implementation involving:

- **Custom binary wire protocol** for control/data plane communication
- **Reverse tunnel establishment** through NAT/firewalls
- **Connection multiplexing** over a single TCP connection
- **TLS termination** at the edge
- **Subdomain routing** with wildcard DNS
- **Request inspection, logging, and replay**
- **Token-based authentication** on tunnels
- **Sliding-window rate limiting**
- **Real-time web dashboard** for monitoring
- **High-concurrency architecture** handling thousands of simultaneous connections

**Tech stack:** Rust (core engine) + Go (dashboard API) + Svelte (dashboard UI) + SQLite (metadata) + Redis (rate limiting & session state)

**Estimated scope:** ~15,000вҖ“25,000 lines of code across all components.

---

---

## 2. Vision & Philosophy

### 2.1 Why Build This?

ngrok is a **$3.2 billion company** (as of 2024). It's one of the most-used developer tools in the world. Every web developer, mobile developer, webhook integrator, and API tester has used it.

And yet, at its core, it's "just" networking. TCP proxying. Reverse tunnels. TLS. Routing. All things that are **buildable** if you understand the fundamentals.

Building D-RAP proves you understand:

| Concept | Depth |
|---|---|
| TCP/IP networking | Socket-level, not library-level |
| NAT traversal | How connections survive firewalls |
| Protocol design | Designing a wire format from scratch |
| Concurrency | Handling 10,000+ simultaneous connections |
| Cryptography (applied) | TLS termination, token auth, certificate management |
| Systems programming | Raw memory management, zero-copy I/O |
| Distributed systems | Relay servers, connection routing, state management |
| Developer tooling | CLI design, DX, documentation |
| Full-stack capability | Backend engine + web dashboard |

### 2.2 Design Principles

1. **Zero Magic**: Every byte on the wire is accounted for. No hidden abstractions.
2. **Performance First**: The relay server should add <5ms latency to proxied requests.
3. **Developer Experience Matters**: The CLI should feel as polished as ngrok's.
4. **Security by Default**: All tunnels use TLS. Auth tokens are non-optional in production mode.
5. **Observability Built In**: Every request is loggable, inspectable, and replayable.
6. **Single Binary Distribution**: The CLI compiles to one binary. No runtime dependencies.

### 2.3 What This Is NOT

- **Not a VPN.** D-RAP tunnels specific ports/services, not entire network interfaces.
- **Not an SSH tunnel wrapper.** The protocol is custom, purpose-built, and more efficient.
- **Not a toy.** This should handle real development workloads вҖ” webhook testing, API development, demo sharing, IoT device exposure.

---

---

## 3. Problem Statement

### 3.1 The Core Problem

A developer runs a web application on `localhost:3000`. They need it accessible from the public internet for:

- **Webhook testing** (Stripe, GitHub, Twilio send events to a public URL)
- **Mobile app development** (phone needs to hit the API running on laptop)
- **Demo sharing** (show a client your WIP without deploying)
- **IoT/embedded** (device behind NAT needs to be reachable)
- **Collaborative debugging** (teammate needs to see your local environment)
- **API integration testing** (third-party service needs to reach your endpoint)

### 3.2 Why This Is Hard

The developer's machine is behind:

```
[Developer's Machine]
        в”Ӯ
   [Home Router / NAT]
        в”Ӯ
   [ISP's CGNAT (possibly)]
        в”Ӯ
   [The Internet]
        в”Ӯ
   [Webhook Sender / Client]
```

**NAT (Network Address Translation)** means the developer's machine doesn't have a public IP address. Incoming connections from the internet cannot reach it directly.

**Traditional solutions and their problems:**

| Solution | Problem |
|---|---|
| Port forwarding on router | Requires router access, static IP, security risk |
| Dynamic DNS | Still requires port forwarding, doesn't solve NAT |
| SSH reverse tunnel | Clunky, no HTTP-specific features, no inspection |
| Deploy to staging | Slow iteration cycle, costs money |
| ngrok | Proprietary, rate-limited on free tier, costs money at scale |

### 3.3 D-RAP's Solution

D-RAP solves this with a **relay architecture**:

```
[localhost:3000] вҶҗTCPвҶ’ [D-RAP Client] в•җв•җв•җTUNNELв•җв•җв•җв–¶ [D-RAP Relay Server] вҶҗHTTPSвҶ’ [Public Internet]
                       (developer's                  (cloud server with             (webhook sender,
                        machine)                      public IP & DNS)               browser, etc.)
```

The key insight: **The D-RAP client initiates the connection outward** (which NAT allows), and then the relay server **reverses the direction** of request flow over that established connection.

---

---

## 4. What D-RAP Does

### 4.1 Feature Matrix

| Feature | Description | Priority |
|---|---|---|
| **HTTP Tunneling** | Expose local HTTP/HTTPS servers via public URL | P0 вҖ” Core |
| **TCP Tunneling** | Expose any TCP service (databases, game servers, SSH) | P0 вҖ” Core |
| **Custom Subdomains** | `drap http 3000 --subdomain=myapp` вҶ’ `myapp.drap.io` | P0 вҖ” Core |
| **Random Subdomains** | Auto-generated: `wild-fox-42.drap.io` | P0 вҖ” Core |
| **TLS Termination** | All public URLs served over HTTPS automatically | P0 вҖ” Core |
| **Request Inspection** | View headers, body, timing of every request in real-time | P1 вҖ” Important |
| **Request Replay** | Re-send any captured request to your local server | P1 вҖ” Important |
| **Rate Limiting** | Protect tunnels from abuse with configurable limits | P1 вҖ” Important |
| **Tunnel Authentication** | Require username/password or token to access tunnel | P1 вҖ” Important |
| **Web Dashboard** | Real-time UI showing tunnels, requests, metrics | P1 вҖ” Important |
| **Multiple Tunnels** | Run several tunnels simultaneously from one client | P2 вҖ” Nice |
| **Config File** | Define tunnels in `drap.yml` instead of CLI args | P2 вҖ” Nice |
| **Wildcard Domains** | `*.myapp.drap.io` routes all subdomains to local | P2 вҖ” Nice |
| **IP Whitelisting** | Only allow specific IPs to access tunnel | P2 вҖ” Nice |
| **Webhook Signature Verification** | Verify webhook authenticity at the relay | P3 вҖ” Future |
| **gRPC Tunneling** | HTTP/2 based gRPC tunnel support | P3 вҖ” Future |
| **UDP Tunneling** | DNS, game servers, VoIP | P3 вҖ” Future |

### 4.2 User Workflows

**Workflow 1: Simple HTTP Tunnel**
```
Developer runs:     $ drap http 3000
Gets URL:           https://abc123.drap.io
Shares URL:         Sends to Stripe webhook config
Stripe sends POST:  POST https://abc123.drap.io/webhook
D-RAP relays:       вҶ’ POST http://localhost:3000/webhook
Developer sees:     Request appears in local server logs + D-RAP dashboard
```

**Workflow 2: Custom Subdomain with Auth**
```
Developer runs:     $ drap http 8080 --subdomain=demo --auth="user:pass123"
Gets URL:           https://demo.drap.io
Client visits:      Browser prompts for Basic Auth
After auth:         Proxied to localhost:8080
```

**Workflow 3: TCP Tunnel for Database**
```
Developer runs:     $ drap tcp 5432
Gets address:       tcp://abc123.drap.io:54320
Teammate connects:  psql -h abc123.drap.io -p 54320 -U postgres
D-RAP relays:       вҶ’ TCP connection to localhost:5432
```

**Workflow 4: Request Inspection & Replay**
```
Developer runs:     $ drap http 3000 --inspect
Dashboard opens:    http://127.0.0.1:4040
Webhook arrives:    POST /api/payment-complete
Developer sees:     Full request in dashboard (headers, body, timing)
Developer clicks:   [Replay] button
Request re-sent:    Same POST hits localhost:3000 again
Developer debugs:   Fixes handler, replays again, confirms fix
```

**Workflow 5: Config File Multi-Tunnel**
```yaml
# drap.yml
authtoken: drap_tok_abc123xyz
tunnels:
  frontend:
    proto: http
    addr: 3000
    subdomain: my-frontend
    inspect: true
  api:
    proto: http
    addr: 8080
    subdomain: my-api
    auth: "admin:secret"
    rate_limit: 100/min
  database:
    proto: tcp
    addr: 5432
```
```
$ drap start --config drap.yml

Tunnels:
  https://my-frontend.drap.io вҶ’ http://localhost:3000
  https://my-api.drap.io      вҶ’ http://localhost:8080
  tcp://rand-slug.drap.io:44301 вҶ’ tcp://localhost:5432
```

```

### 5.2 Component Map

```
D-RAP
в”ңв”Җв”Җ drap-client/          # CLI client binary (Rust)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ drap-server/          # Relay server binary (Rust)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ drap-protocol/        # Shared wire protocol library (Rust)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ drap-dashboard-api/   # Dashboard REST + WebSocket API (Go)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ drap-dashboard-ui/    # Dashboard web frontend (Svelte)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ drap-common/          # Shared types, crypto utils (Rust)
в””в”Җв”Җ drap-tests/           # Integration & load tests
```

### 5.3 Data Flow вҖ” HTTP Request Lifecycle

```
Step 1:  Client app starts, connects to relay server via TLS
Step 2:  Client sends AUTH frame with token
Step 3:  Server validates token, sends AUTH_OK
Step 4:  Client sends TUNNEL_REQ (proto=HTTP, subdomain="myapp")
Step 5:  Server checks subdomain availability
Step 6:  Server registers subdomain in routing table
Step 7:  Server sends TUNNEL_CREATED (url="https://myapp.drap.io")
Step 8:  Client displays URL to developer
         --- Tunnel is now established ---

Step 9:  External client sends: GET https://myapp.drap.io/api/users
Step 10: Relay server terminates TLS
Step 11: Subdomain router matches "myapp" вҶ’ Tunnel #X
Step 12: Rate limiter checks: within limits? вң“
Step 13: Auth gate checks: auth required? (if yes, validate)
Step 14: Request inspector logs the full request
Step 15: Server creates DATA frame with request bytes
Step 16: Server sends DATA frame over multiplexed tunnel connection
Step 17: Client receives DATA frame
Step 18: Client demultiplexes: this is for stream #42
Step 19: Client opens TCP connection to localhost:3000
Step 20: Client forwards request bytes to localhost:3000
Step 21: Local app processes request, sends response
Step 22: Client reads response from localhost:3000
Step 23: Client wraps response in DATA frame (stream #42)
Step 24: Client sends DATA frame back to relay server
Step 25: Server demultiplexes: stream #42
Step 26: Request inspector logs the full response
Step 27: Server sends HTTP response to external client
Step 28: Dashboard updates in real-time via WebSocket
```

**Total added latency target: <5ms** (excluding network transit time)

---

---

## 6. Tech Stack Decision

### 6.1 Decision Matrix

| Component | Language/Tech | Why This Over Alternatives |
|---|---|---|
| **CLI Client** | **Rust** | Single binary, zero runtime deps, raw socket access, memory safety without GC pauses, async ecosystem (tokio) |
| **Relay Server** | **Rust** | Same reasons + needs maximum performance for high concurrency proxy workload |
| **Wire Protocol** | **Custom binary (Rust)** | Need control over every byte; no existing protocol fits exactly |
| **Dashboard API** | **Go** | Fast HTTP server, great for WebSocket handling, lighter weight than Rust for a CRUD API layer |
| **Dashboard UI** | **Svelte** | Minimal bundle size, reactive by default, no virtual DOM overhead, perfect for real-time dashboards |
| **Metadata Store** | **SQLite** | Embedded, zero-config, file-based, perfect for local client state + server metadata |
| **Session/Rate Limit Store** | **Redis** | In-memory speed, built-in TTL, atomic counters, pub/sub for multi-instance relay servers |
| **TLS** | **rustls** | Pure-Rust TLS, no OpenSSL dependency hell, audited, modern |
| **Async Runtime** | **tokio** | Industry-standard async runtime for Rust, work-stealing scheduler, io_uring support |
| **Serialization** | **Custom binary + serde/JSON for API** | Binary for wire protocol (speed), JSON for REST API (interop) |
| **Testing** | **Rust's built-in + Go test + Playwright** | Unit tests in respective languages, E2E with Playwright for dashboard |
| **CI/CD** | **GitHub Actions** | Standard, free for open-source, great Rust/Go support |
| **Deployment** | **Single binary + Docker** | Distribute CLI as single binary, relay server as Docker container |

### 6.2 Why Rust for the Core?

This is a networking-heavy, performance-critical system. The relay server might handle **thousands of concurrent tunnels**, each with **hundreds of concurrent requests**. Every microsecond of latency matters. Every byte of memory matters.

**Rust gives us:**

1. **Zero-cost abstractions** вҖ” Generics, traits, iterators compile to the same code you'd write in C
2. **No garbage collector** вҖ” No GC pauses means predictable latency (critical for a proxy)
3. **Ownership model** вҖ” Prevents data races at compile time (critical for concurrent networking)
4. **async/await + tokio** вҖ” Handles millions of concurrent connections with minimal threads
5. **Single binary** вҖ” `cargo build --release` produces one file, cross-compile for any platform
6. **Ecosystem** вҖ” `tokio`, `rustls`, `hyper`, `bytes`, `tracing` are battle-tested
7. **Memory safety** вҖ” A proxy handles untrusted input; buffer overflows are unacceptable

**Why not Go?** Go would be the second choice. Its goroutine model is great for concurrency, but:
- GC pauses can cause tail latency spikes in the proxy path
- Less control over memory layout
- Larger binary sizes
- We use Go for the dashboard API where these tradeoffs are acceptable

**Why not C/C++?** We already proved we can write C (OS project). Rust gives us the same performance with safety guarantees. In a networking proxy that handles untrusted input, safety is non-negotiable.

### 6.3 Why Go for the Dashboard API?

The dashboard API is a standard REST + WebSocket server. It doesn't need Rust's performance. Go gives us:
- Faster development for CRUD operations
- `net/http` is excellent out of the box
- `gorilla/websocket` is mature
- JSON handling is trivial
- Smaller cognitive overhead for a simpler component

### 6.4 Why Svelte for the Dashboard UI?

The dashboard is a real-time monitoring tool. It needs to:
- Update live as requests flow through
- Display request/response bodies (potentially large)
- Feel snappy and responsive
- Have minimal bundle size (served from the CLI client locally)

Svelte compiles to vanilla JS with no runtime library. The bundle will be tiny. Reactivity is built into the language. Perfect fit.

### 6.5 Dependency Policy

**Allowed dependencies (Rust):**
- `tokio` вҖ” Async runtime (not reinventing an event loop)
- `rustls` / `tokio-rustls` вҖ” TLS (not reimplementing crypto)
- `bytes` вҖ” Efficient byte buffer management
- `tracing` вҖ” Structured logging
- `clap` вҖ” CLI argument parsing
- `serde` вҖ” Serialization framework
- `uuid` вҖ” ID generation
- `dashmap` вҖ” Concurrent hash map
- `sqlx` вҖ” SQLite async driver

**NOT allowed:**
- `hyper` вҖ” We're building our own HTTP parser
- `axum` / `warp` / `actix` вҖ” We're building our own server
- Any tunneling library вҖ” That's the whole point
- Any proxy library вҖ” Same

**The HTTP parsing, proxying, tunneling, multiplexing, and protocol handling are all built from scratch.** Libraries are only used for things outside the project's learning scope (TLS crypto, async runtime, CLI parsing).

---

---

## 7. Core Components Deep Dive

### 7.1 D-RAP CLI Client

**Responsibility:** The binary that runs on the developer's machine. Establishes tunnel connections, proxies traffic between local services and the relay server.

**Sub-components:**

```
drap-client/
в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.rs                    # Entry point, CLI parsing
в”ңв”Җв”Җ config/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cli_args.rs            # clap argument definitions
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ file_config.rs         # drap.yml parser
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ merged_config.rs       # CLI args + file config merge logic
в”ңв”Җв”Җ auth/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ token_store.rs         # Persist auth token to ~/.drap/authtoken
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ authenticator.rs       # Handle auth flow with relay server
в”ңв”Җв”Җ tunnel/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tunnel_manager.rs      # Manages lifecycle of all tunnels
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ http_tunnel.rs         # HTTP-specific tunnel logic
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tcp_tunnel.rs          # TCP-specific tunnel logic
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tunnel_state.rs        # State machine for tunnel lifecycle
в”ңв”Җв”Җ connection/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ control_connection.rs  # Single persistent connection to relay
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ multiplexer.rs         # Stream multiplexing over control conn
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ reconnector.rs         # Auto-reconnect with exponential backoff
в”ңв”Җв”Җ proxy/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ local_proxy.rs         # Connects to localhost services
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ http_proxy.rs          # HTTP request/response forwarding
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tcp_proxy.rs           # Raw TCP byte forwarding
в”ңв”Җв”Җ inspector/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ request_logger.rs      # Captures requests for inspection
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ replay_engine.rs       # Re-sends captured requests
в”ңв”Җв”Җ dashboard/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ local_server.rs        # HTTP server on :4040
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ websocket.rs           # Live updates to dashboard UI
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ static_assets.rs       # Embedded Svelte build
в””в”Җв”Җ display/
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ terminal_ui.rs         # Pretty terminal output
    в””в”Җв”Җ status_display.rs      # Live connection status
```

**Key Design Decisions:**

1. **Single persistent control connection:** The client maintains exactly ONE TLS connection to the relay server. All tunnels are multiplexed over this connection. This minimizes resource usage and NAT mapping entries.

2. **Lazy local connections:** The client does NOT pre-connect to localhost services. It connects to `localhost:3000` only when a request arrives that needs to be forwarded. Connections are pooled and reused.

3. **Embedded dashboard:** The Svelte dashboard UI is compiled and embedded directly into the Rust binary using `include_bytes!()`. No external files needed.

4. **Graceful shutdown:** SIGINT/SIGTERM triggers: close all tunnels вҶ’ send TUNNEL_CLOSE frames вҶ’ drain in-flight requests (5s timeout) вҶ’ close control connection вҶ’ exit.

### 7.2 D-RAP Relay Server

**Responsibility:** The cloud-hosted server with a public IP. Accepts incoming tunnel connections from clients. Accepts incoming HTTP/TCP connections from the public internet. Routes public traffic to the correct tunnel.

**Sub-components:**

```
drap-server/
в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.rs
в”ңв”Җв”Җ config/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ server_config.rs       # Port bindings, domain, TLS certs, limits
в”ңв”Җв”Җ listener/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tls_acceptor.rs        # TLS termination for public HTTPS
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ http_listener.rs       # Accept public HTTP connections (port 443)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tcp_listener.rs        # Accept public TCP connections (port range)
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ control_listener.rs    # Accept tunnel client connections (port 4443)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ router/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ subdomain_router.rs    # Map subdomain вҶ’ tunnel
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tcp_port_router.rs     # Map public port вҶ’ tunnel
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ routing_table.rs       # Thread-safe routing table (DashMap)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ tunnel/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tunnel_registry.rs     # All active tunnels
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tunnel_session.rs      # State per connected client
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tunnel_allocator.rs    # Assign subdomains, TCP ports
в”ңв”Җв”Җ proxy/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ http_proxy.rs          # Parse HTTP, forward via tunnel, return response
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tcp_proxy.rs           # Raw byte forwarding via tunnel
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ bidirectional_copy.rs  # Efficient async bidirectional byte copy
в”ңв”Җв”Җ connection/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ control_handler.rs     # Handle D-RAP protocol messages
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ multiplexer.rs         # Server-side stream multiplexing
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ connection_pool.rs     # Pool connections per tunnel
в”ңв”Җв”Җ security/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ auth_gate.rs           # Tunnel-level authentication (Basic Auth, token)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ rate_limiter.rs        # Sliding window rate limiting
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ip_whitelist.rs        # IP-based access control
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ token_validator.rs     # Validate client auth tokens
в”ңв”Җв”Җ inspector/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ request_capture.rs     # Capture full req/res for inspection
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ storage.rs             # Store captured requests (SQLite + in-memory ring buffer)
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ replay.rs              # Replay request through tunnel
в”ңв”Җв”Җ metrics/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ counter.rs             # Request counts, byte counts
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ latency.rs             # Request latency histograms
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ exporter.rs            # Expose metrics for dashboard
в””в”Җв”Җ admin/
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ mod.rs
    в””в”Җв”Җ management_api.rs      # Internal API for tunnel management
```

**Key Design Decisions:**

1. **Separate listener ports:**
   - Port `443` вҖ” Public HTTPS traffic (subdomain-routed)
   - Port `4443` вҖ” D-RAP client control connections
   - Ports `40000-50000` вҖ” Public TCP tunnel endpoints
   This separation ensures the relay server can independently scale and secure each listener.

2. **Shared-nothing tunnel sessions:** Each connected client gets its own `TunnelSession` with its own multiplexer state. Sessions don't interact directly вҖ” only through the routing table.

3. **Lock-free routing table:** The subdomain routing table uses `DashMap` (sharded concurrent hash map) for lock-free reads. Subdomain lookups happen on every incoming request вҖ” they must be O(1) and lock-free.

4. **Horizontal scalability consideration:** While V1 is a single relay server, the architecture is designed so that multiple relay servers could share state via Redis and a global routing layer (future).

### 7.3 D-RAP Dashboard

**Architecture:**

```
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

**Dashboard Pages:**

1. **Overview** вҖ” Active tunnels, total requests, current throughput graph
2. **Tunnel Detail** вҖ” URL, status, uptime, recent requests for this tunnel
3. **Request Inspector** вҖ” Filterable list of all requests. Click to expand: headers, body (formatted JSON/XML), timing breakdown, response
4. **Replay** вҖ” Button on each request to re-send it. Shows replay result side-by-side with original
5. **Settings** вҖ” Rate limit config, auth config, IP whitelist management

### 7.4 Control Plane Protocol

The **control plane** is how the CLI client and relay server communicate about tunnel lifecycle вҖ” creating tunnels, destroying tunnels, authentication, heartbeats, errors.

**This uses the D-RAP Wire Protocol (Section 9) with specific control frame types.**

```
Control Plane Messages:

CLIENT вҶ’ SERVER:
  AUTH_REQ          вҶ’ Authenticate with token
  TUNNEL_REQ        вҶ’ Request a new tunnel
  TUNNEL_CLOSE      вҶ’ Close an existing tunnel
  HEARTBEAT_PONG    вҶ’ Respond to heartbeat
  
SERVER вҶ’ CLIENT:
  AUTH_OK           вҶ’ Authentication successful
  AUTH_FAIL         вҶ’ Authentication failed (reason)
  TUNNEL_CREATED    вҶ’ Tunnel established (URL, port info)
  TUNNEL_DENIED     вҶ’ Tunnel request denied (subdomain taken, limit reached)
  TUNNEL_CLOSED_ACK вҶ’ Confirmed tunnel closed
  HEARTBEAT_PING    вҶ’ Are you alive?
  ERROR             вҶ’ General error
  SERVER_SHUTDOWN   вҶ’ Server is shutting down, reconnect
```

**Control connection lifecycle:**

```
Client                                    Server
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ TCP Connect в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ TLS Handshake в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ AUTH_REQ {token: "drap_tok_..."} в”Җв”ҖвҶ’в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җ AUTH_OK {user: "dev@axiom.io"} в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_REQ {proto: HTTP,           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      subdomain: "myapp"} в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_CREATED {                    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      tunnel_id: "t_abc123",            в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ      url: "https://myapp.drap.io"} в”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ         ... tunnel is live ...           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җ HEARTBEAT_PING в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ HEARTBEAT_PONG в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ         ... heartbeat every 30s ...     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_CLOSE {id: "t_abc123"} в”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_CLOSED_ACK в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ TCP FIN в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
```

### 7.5 Data Plane & Tunneling Engine

The **data plane** is how actual HTTP/TCP traffic flows between the relay server and the CLI client. This is the performance-critical path.

**Design: Multiplexed Streams Over Single Connection**

Rather than opening a new TCP connection for every proxied request, D-RAP multiplexes all traffic over the **single control connection** using **stream IDs** (similar to HTTP/2's multiplexing concept).

```
Single TCP Connection (TLS):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Stream 1: GET /api/users      вҶ’ Response     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Stream 2: POST /webhook       вҶ’ Response     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Stream 3: GET /health         вҶ’ Response     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Stream 4: [TCP bytes for DB connection]      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Stream 5: GET /api/orders     вҶ’ Response     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Control:  HEARTBEAT_PING / PONG              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Control:  TUNNEL_REQ / TUNNEL_CREATED        в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

Each stream has:
- A unique 32-bit stream ID
- A tunnel ID (which tunnel this stream belongs to)
- A state machine: OPEN вҶ’ DATA_FLOWING вҶ’ HALF_CLOSED вҶ’ CLOSED
- Flow control: per-stream window size to prevent a slow local service from blocking other streams

**Why multiplexing over a single connection?**

1. **NAT mapping preservation:** NAT tables have limited entries. One connection = one entry.
2. **Fewer TLS handshakes:** TLS handshake is expensive (~2 RTT). We do it once.
3. **Simpler firewall traversal:** Only one outbound connection to manage.
4. **Resource efficiency:** Fewer file descriptors, fewer TCP buffers.

**Tradeoff:** Head-of-line blocking on the TCP level. If one packet is lost, all streams are blocked until retransmission. This is the same tradeoff HTTP/2 makes. Acceptable for our use case.

### 7.6 Subdomain Router

**Responsibility:** When a request arrives at `https://myapp.drap.io/some/path`, determine which tunnel it should be routed to.

**Implementation approach:**

```
Incoming request:
  Host: myapp.drap.io

Router logic:
  1. Extract Host header
  2. Parse subdomain: "myapp" from "myapp.drap.io"
  3. Lookup in routing table: subdomain_map["myapp"] вҶ’ TunnelSession #42
  4. If not found вҶ’ return 502 "Tunnel not found"
  5. If found but tunnel is disconnected вҶ’ return 504 "Tunnel offline"
  6. Forward to TunnelSession #42's multiplexer
```

**DNS Setup:**
```
*.drap.io  A     <relay-server-IP>
*.drap.io  AAAA  <relay-server-IPv6>
drap.io    A     <relay-server-IP>
```

A wildcard DNS record means ALL subdomains resolve to the relay server. The relay server then routes based on the subdomain.

**TLS for Wildcard:**
A wildcard TLS certificate (`*.drap.io`) covers all subdomains. One certificate, unlimited tunnels.

**Subdomain Allocation Rules:**
- Reserved words: `www`, `api`, `admin`, `dashboard`, `status`, `mail`, etc.
- Custom subdomains: first-come-first-served, must be 3-63 chars, alphanumeric + hyphens
- Random subdomains: adjective-noun-number format (`wild-fox-42`)
- Subdomain expires when tunnel closes (not reserved permanently on free tier)

### 7.7 TLS Termination Layer

**Where TLS happens:**

```
Public Client  в”Җв”ҖHTTPSв”Җв”Җв–¶  [Relay Server: TLS Termination]  в”Җв”ҖPlaintextв”Җв”Җв–¶  [Tunnel Mux]
                                                                                 в”Ӯ
                                                                           D-RAP Protocol
                                                                           (over TLS)
                                                                                 в”Ӯ
                                                                          [CLI Client]
                                                                                 в”Ӯ
                                                                         в”Җв”ҖPlaintextв”Җв”Җв–¶
                                                                          localhost:3000
```

**Two TLS contexts on the relay server:**

1. **Public-facing TLS** (port 443): Uses wildcard cert `*.drap.io`. Terminates HTTPS from browsers/webhooks/clients. Standard TLS 1.3.

2. **Client-facing TLS** (port 4443): Uses server cert for `relay.drap.io`. Authenticates the relay server to CLI clients. The CLI client validates this cert. Could add mTLS for client certificates in the future.

**Certificate management:**
- V1: Manual certificate (Let's Encrypt wildcard via DNS challenge)
- Future: ACME integration for automatic renewal
- Certificate stored on disk, loaded into `rustls::ServerConfig` at startup
- Hot-reloading: watch cert files for changes, swap `ServerConfig` atomically

### 7.8 Authentication & Authorization System

**Two levels of authentication:**

**Level 1: Client Authentication (Who are you?)**
```
When: Client connects to relay server
How:  AUTH_REQ frame with auth token
Token format: drap_tok_<base64(random 32 bytes)>
Storage: ~/.drap/authtoken on client, users table in server's SQLite
Verification: Constant-time comparison on server
```

**Level 2: Tunnel Authentication (Who can access your tunnel?)**
```
When: Public user accesses a tunnel URL
Options:
  a) None (public, default)
  b) HTTP Basic Auth (username:password, set by tunnel owner)
  c) Bearer Token (X-Drap-Token header)
  d) IP Whitelist (only specific IPs can access)
  e) OAuth2 (future: GitHub, Google login to access tunnel)
```

**Auth flow for Basic Auth on tunnels:**

```
Browser вҶ’ GET https://myapp.drap.io
Relay   вҶ’ 401 Unauthorized, WWW-Authenticate: Basic realm="D-RAP Tunnel"
Browser вҶ’ GET (with Authorization: Basic base64(user:pass))
Relay   вҶ’ Validates credentials against tunnel config
        вҶ’ If valid: proxy request to tunnel
        вҶ’ If invalid: 403 Forbidden
```

### 7.9 Rate Limiter

**Algorithm: Sliding Window Log with Token Bucket Hybrid**

Why not just token bucket? We want precise per-second granularity AND burst tolerance.

**Implementation:**

```
For each tunnel:
  - Configurable rate: X requests per Y seconds (e.g., 100 req/min)
  - Burst allowance: Z requests above limit in short burst (e.g., 20)
  
Storage: Redis
  Key: rate:{tunnel_id}
  Value: Sorted set of timestamps

Check logic:
  1. Current time = now
  2. Remove entries older than window (now - Y seconds)
  3. Count remaining entries
  4. If count < X + Z: ALLOW, add timestamp
  5. Else: DENY, return 429 Too Many Requests

Response headers:
  X-RateLimit-Limit: 100
  X-RateLimit-Remaining: 42
  X-RateLimit-Reset: 1699999999
  Retry-After: 30 (if rate limited)
```

**Rate limiting layers:**
1. **Global server rate limit:** Protects the relay server itself (e.g., 10,000 req/s total)
2. **Per-account rate limit:** Free tier vs paid tier limits
3. **Per-tunnel rate limit:** Configurable by the tunnel owner
4. **Per-IP rate limit:** Prevents a single source from abusing a tunnel

### 7.10 Request Inspector & Replay Engine

**What gets captured (for HTTP tunnels with inspection enabled):**

```
CapturedRequest {
    id: UUID,
    tunnel_id: String,
    timestamp: DateTime,
    duration_ms: u64,
    
    request: {
        method: String,          // "POST"
        url: String,             // "/api/webhook"
        headers: Map<String, String>,
        body: Bytes,             // Raw body
        body_size: u64,
        content_type: String,    // "application/json"
        remote_addr: IpAddr,
    },
    
    response: {
        status_code: u16,        // 200
        headers: Map<String, String>,
        body: Bytes,
        body_size: u64,
        content_type: String,
    },
    
    timing: {
        dns_ms: u64,             // 0 (not applicable for proxy)
        tls_ms: u64,             // TLS termination time
        tunnel_rtt_ms: u64,      // Time to reach client through tunnel
        local_processing_ms: u64, // Time local server took to respond
        total_ms: u64,
    }
}
```

**Storage strategy:**
- **Hot storage:** In-memory ring buffer, last 500 requests per tunnel. Zero-latency access for dashboard.
- **Warm storage:** SQLite on relay server. Last 24 hours of requests. Queryable.
- **Body storage:** Bodies > 1MB are stored to disk, referenced by path. Bodies > 10MB are not captured (configurable).

**Replay engine:**

```
User clicks "Replay" on request #abc123 in dashboard:

1. Dashboard UI вҶ’ POST /api/requests/abc123/replay
2. Dashboard API вҶ’ Reads original request from storage
3. Dashboard API вҶ’ Sends replay command to relay server via internal channel
4. Relay server вҶ’ Creates new DATA frame with original request bytes
5. Relay server вҶ’ Sends through tunnel to CLI client
6. CLI client вҶ’ Forwards to localhost:3000
7. Response flows back
8. New CapturedRequest created with is_replay: true
9. Dashboard shows original and replay side-by-side
```

### 7.11 Connection Pool Manager

**Two connection pools exist:**

**Pool 1: CLI Client вҶ’ Local Services**

```
The client maintains a pool of TCP connections to each local address.

localhost:3000 pool:
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ Connection A (idle, keepalive)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ Connection B (active, streaming response)
  в””в”Җв”Җ Connection C (idle, keepalive)

Pool config:
  - min_idle: 2
  - max_connections: 50
  - idle_timeout: 60s
  - connect_timeout: 5s
  
On incoming proxied request:
  1. Try to acquire idle connection from pool
  2. If available: use it, send request
  3. If not available and pool < max: create new connection
  4. If pool at max: queue request, wait up to 5s
  5. If timeout: return 502 to relay server
  
Connection health:
  - Check connection is still alive before use (TCP keepalive)
  - If connection reset mid-request: retry once with new connection
  - Remove broken connections from pool
```

**Pool 2: Relay Server вҖ” Managed Implicitly**

The relay server doesn't pool connections TO clients (the tunnel IS the connection). But it pools internal resources:
- Redis connection pool (for rate limiting)
- SQLite connection pool (for request storage)
- Pre-allocated byte buffers for frame parsing (object pool pattern)

---

---

## 8. Networking Deep Dive

### 8.1 NAT Traversal Strategy

**The problem:**
```
Developer's machine: 192.168.1.100 (private IP)
Router's public IP:  73.42.198.55
                     But which port? NAT mapping is unpredictable.
                     And incoming connections are blocked by default.
```

**D-RAP's approach: Outbound-Only Connection**

We don't try to punch through NAT. We don't use STUN/TURN/ICE. Instead:

```
Strategy: The client ALWAYS initiates the connection outward.

1. Client connects to relay server (outbound TCP on port 4443)
   вҶ’ NAT creates mapping: 192.168.1.100:54321 вҶ” 73.42.198.55:54321 вҶ’ relay:4443
   
2. This connection stays open (persistent, keepalive)

3. When public traffic arrives at relay server, it's forwarded 
   OVER THIS EXISTING CONNECTION back to the client

4. NAT sees this as response traffic on an established connection
   вҶ’ Allowed through without any configuration
```

This is why D-RAP works behind:
- Home routers
- Corporate firewalls
- Hotel/airport WiFi
- CGNAT (carrier-grade NAT)
- Multiple layers of NAT

**The only requirement:** The client can make outbound TCP connections on port 4443 (or configurable). This works ~99.9% of the time.

### 8.2 Reverse Tunneling Mechanism

**Detailed reverse tunnel flow:**

```
Phase 1: Tunnel Establishment (Client вҶ’ Server)
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

Client                          Server
  в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ SYN в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ  TCP handshake
  в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ SYN-ACK в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ ACK в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ Finished в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ    [TLS established]           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ AUTH_REQ(token) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ  D-RAP auth
  в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ AUTH_OK в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_REQ(HTTP,"myapp")в”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ  Request tunnel
  в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_CREATED(url) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ    [Tunnel is now LIVE]        в”Ӯ


Phase 2: Reverse Traffic Flow (Server вҶ’ Client вҶ’ localhost)
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җ HTTPS GET в”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ TLS terminate             в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ Route: "myapp" вҶ’ tunnel   в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ Rate limit: OK            в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җ DATA(stream=1, в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ    request bytes)         в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җ HTTP GET в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҖвҶ’ в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ HTTP 200 в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ DATA(stream=1, в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ     response bytes)       в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ вҶҗв”Җв”Җ HTTPS 200 в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
    в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ
```

**Key insight:** The "reverse" part is that data flows SERVER вҶ’ CLIENT over an existing connection. Normally, the client initiates data flow. Here, the server pushes data to the client. The client then acts as a local proxy to the developer's application.

### 8.3 Connection Multiplexing

**Why multiplexing?**

Without multiplexing:
```
Request 1: [Open TCP] [TLS Handshake] [Send Request] [Get Response] [Close TCP]
Request 2: [Open TCP] [TLS Handshake] [Send Request] [Get Response] [Close TCP]
Request 3: [Open TCP] [TLS Handshake] [Send Request] [Get Response] [Close TCP]
```

With multiplexing:
```
Single connection:
  Stream 1: [Send Request] в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ [Get Response]
  Stream 2:      [Send Request] в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ [Get Response]
  Stream 3:           [Send Request] в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ [Get Response]
```

**D-RAP multiplexing design (inspired by HTTP/2, simplified):**

```
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ              Single TCP Connection            в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                               в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”ӮStream 1 в”Ӯ в”ӮStream 2 в”Ӯ в”ӮStream 3 в”Ӯ  ...   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ(req #1) в”Ӯ в”Ӯ(req #2) в”Ӯ в”Ӯ(req #3) в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ               в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ       в–ј           в–ј           в–ј               в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ     в”Ӯ

               в–ј
        в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
        в”Ӯ   CLOSED     в”Ӯ
        в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

**Flow control:**
- Each stream has a window size (default: 64KB)
- Sender cannot send more bytes than the receiver's advertised window
- Receiver sends WINDOW_UPDATE frames to increase the window
- Prevents a slow consumer from causing unbounded buffering

**Max concurrent streams:** 256 per tunnel connection (configurable)

### 8.4 TCP Proxy Architecture

For TCP tunnels (databases, game servers, SSH, etc.), D-RAP acts as a raw byte proxy вҖ” no HTTP parsing, no inspection, just bidirectional byte forwarding.

```
Public TCP Client в—Җв•җв•җв•җв–¶ Relay Server в—Җв•җв•җв•җTUNNELв•җв•җв•җв–¶ CLI Client в—Җв•җв•җв•җв–¶ localhost:5432
```

**How TCP tunneling differs from HTTP tunneling:**

| Aspect | HTTP Tunnel | TCP Tunnel |
|---|---|---|
| Public endpoint | `https://sub.drap.io` (port 443) | `tcp://sub.drap.io:44301` (random high port) |
| Protocol awareness | Parses HTTP requests/responses | No parsing, raw bytes |
| Inspection | Full request/response capture | Byte count only |
| Multiplexing | Many HTTP requests per stream | One TCP connection per stream |
| Connection lifecycle | Short-lived (request/response) | Long-lived (persistent connection) |

**TCP port allocation:**
```
Port range: 40000 - 50000 (10,000 ports)
Allocation: Random available port from range
Release: When tunnel closes
Tracking: HashMap<u16, TunnelId> on relay server
```

**Bidirectional byte copying:**

The core of TCP proxying is an efficient bidirectional copy loop:

```
Conceptually:

loop {
    select! {
        // Data from public client вҶ’ send through tunnel to CLI client
        bytes = public_socket.read() => {
            tunnel.send_data(stream_id, bytes).await;
        }
        
        // Data from tunnel (CLI client's local service) вҶ’ send to public client
        frame = tunnel.receive_data(stream_id) => {
            public_socket.write(frame.payload).await;
        }
    }
}
```

In Rust with tokio, this is implemented using `tokio::io::copy_bidirectional` semantics with custom frame wrapping/unwrapping.

### 8.5 Keep-Alive & Heartbeat Protocol

**Problem:** TCP connections through NAT can be silently dropped if idle for too long. NAT tables have timeouts (commonly 60-300 seconds).

**Solution:** Application-level heartbeat protocol.

```
Every 30 seconds:
  Server вҶ’ Client: HEARTBEAT_PING { timestamp: 1699999999 }
  Client вҶ’ Server: HEARTBEAT_PONG { timestamp: 1699999999, client_time: 1699999998 }

If no PONG received within 10 seconds:
  Server marks tunnel as STALE
  After 3 missed heartbeats (90 seconds):
    Server closes tunnel, removes from routing table
    
If no PING received by client within 60 seconds:
  Client assumes connection lost
  Client begins reconnection with exponential backoff:
    Attempt 1: wait 1s
    Attempt 2: wait 2s
    Attempt 3: wait 4s
    Attempt 4: wait 8s
    ...up to max 60s between attempts
    Jitter: Вұ25% on each wait time
```

**Heartbeat data also serves as:**
- RTT measurement (server вҶ’ client вҶ’ server)
- Clock skew detection (comparing timestamps)
- Connection quality monitoring (track consecutive misses)

---

---

## 9. Protocol Design

### 9.1 D-RAP Wire Protocol

D-RAP uses a **custom binary protocol** for communication between CLI client and relay server. This is the heart of the system.

**Why custom instead of HTTP/2 or gRPC?**

| Option | Why Not |
|---|---|
| HTTP/2 | Close, but too heavyweight. We don't need HPACK, pseudo-headers, or HTTP semantics on the control plane |
| gRPC | Requires HTTP/2, adds Protobuf overhead, overkill for our frame types |
| WebSocket | Text-oriented, framing overhead, would need custom binary protocol on top anyway |
| Raw TCP | No framing. We'd need to build framing anyway. |
| QUIC | Would solve head-of-line blocking but adds massive complexity (UDP, custom congestion control) |

D-RAP's protocol is purpose-built: minimal overhead, binary-efficient, multiplexing-aware, and exactly the right abstraction level for tunneling.

### 9.2 Frame Types

**Frame header (fixed 9 bytes, inspired by HTTP/2):**
```
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ  Length (3 bytes)  в”Ӯ  Type (1 byte)  в”Ӯ  Flags (1 byte)  в”Ӯ  Stream ID (4 bytes)  в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
в”Ӯ                         Payload (variable)                       в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Total header: 9 bytes
Max payload: 16,777,215 bytes (2^24 - 1, ~16MB)
Default max payload: 65,535 bytes (64KB) вҖ” configurable via SETTINGS
```

**Frame type definitions:**

```
Type ID в”Ӯ Name              в”Ӯ Direction       в”Ӯ Purpose
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
0x00    в”Ӯ DATA              в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Tunnel payload (HTTP/TCP bytes)
0x01    в”Ӯ HEADERS           в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ HTTP headers (for inspection)
0x02    в”Ӯ RST_STREAM        в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Abort a single stream
0x03    в”Ӯ SETTINGS          в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Connection-level config
0x04    в”Ӯ PING              в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ Heartbeat ping
0x05    в”Ӯ PONG              в”Ӯ ClientвҶ’Server   в”Ӯ Heartbeat pong
0x06    в”Ӯ WINDOW_UPDATE     в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Flow control window increase
0x07    в”Ӯ AUTH_REQ          в”Ӯ ClientвҶ’Server   в”Ӯ Authentication request
0x08    в”Ӯ AUTH_OK           в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ Authentication success
0x09    в”Ӯ AUTH_FAIL         в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ Authentication failure
0x0A    в”Ӯ TUNNEL_REQ        в”Ӯ ClientвҶ’Server   в”Ӯ Request new tunnel
0x0B    в”Ӯ TUNNEL_CREATED    в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ Tunnel established
0x0C    в”Ӯ TUNNEL_DENIED     в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ Tunnel request rejected
0x0D    в”Ӯ TUNNEL_CLOSE      в”Ӯ ClientвҶ’Server   в”Ӯ Close tunnel request
0x0E    в”Ӯ TUNNEL_CLOSED_ACK в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ Tunnel closed confirmation
0x0F    в”Ӯ STREAM_OPEN       в”Ӯ ServerвҶ’Client   в”Ӯ New proxied request incoming
0x10    в”Ӯ STREAM_CLOSE      в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Stream finished
0x11    в”Ӯ ERROR             в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Error with code and message
0x12    в”Ӯ GOAWAY            в”Ӯ Bidirectional   в”Ӯ Graceful shutdown
```

**Frame flags (bitmask):**

```
Bit 0 (0x01): END_STREAM    вҖ” Last frame for this stream
Bit 1 (0x02): END_HEADERS   вҖ” Complete header block
Bit 2 (0x04): PADDED        вҖ” Payload is padded (for traffic analysis resistance)
Bit 3 (0x08): PRIORITY      вҖ” Stream has priority information
Bit 4 (0x10): COMPRESSED    вҖ” Payload is zstd compressed
Bit 5 (0x20): ACK           вҖ” Frame is acknowledgment
Bits 6-7:     Reserved
```

**Detailed frame payloads:**

```
AUTH_REQ (0x07):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Token Length (2 bytes)               в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Token (variable, UTF-8)             в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Client Version (2 bytes, major.minor)в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ OS (1 byte: 0=Linux,1=Mac,2=Win)    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Capabilities Bitmask (2 bytes)       в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

AUTH_OK (0x08):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Session ID (16 bytes, UUID)          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Account Name Length (2 bytes)        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Account Name (variable, UTF-8)       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Max Tunnels (2 bytes)                в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Max Bandwidth (4 bytes, bytes/sec)   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Server Version (2 bytes)             в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

AUTH_FAIL (0x09):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Error Code (2 bytes)                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Reason Length (2 bytes)              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Reason (variable, UTF-8)            в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
  Error codes: 
    0x01 = INVALID_TOKEN
    0x02 = TOKEN_EXPIRED
    0x03 = ACCOUNT_SUSPENDED
    0x04 = VERSION_MISMATCH

TUNNEL_REQ (0x0A):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Protocol (1 byte: 0=HTTP, 1=TCP)     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Local Port (2 bytes)                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Subdomain Length (1 byte)            в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Subdomain (variable, UTF-8, 0=random)в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Options Bitmask (2 bytes)            в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Bit 0: Inspect enabled             в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Bit 1: Auth required               в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Bit 2: Rate limit enabled          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Bit 3: IP whitelist enabled        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If auth]: Auth Type (1 byte)        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   0=Basic, 1=Bearer                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If auth]: Credentials Length (2 b)  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If auth]: Credentials (variable)    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If rate limit]: Limit (4 bytes)     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If rate limit]: Window sec (2 bytes)в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If IP whitelist]: Count (2 bytes)   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If IP whitelist]: IPs (4/16 bytes each) в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

TUNNEL_CREATED (0x0B):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Tunnel ID (16 bytes, UUID)           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Public URL Length (2 bytes)          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Public URL (variable, UTF-8)         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If TCP]: Assigned Port (2 bytes)    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Assigned Subdomain Length (1 byte)   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Assigned Subdomain (variable)        в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

DATA (0x00):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ [If PADDED]: Pad Length (1 byte)     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Payload (variable)                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If PADDED]: Padding (variable, 0s) в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
  Stream ID in header identifies which request/connection
  END_STREAM flag indicates last DATA frame

STREAM_OPEN (0x0F):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Tunnel ID (16 bytes)                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Remote Addr Length (1 byte)          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Remote Addr (variable, IP string)    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Remote Port (2 bytes)                в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If HTTP]: Method Length (1 byte)    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If HTTP]: Method (variable)         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If HTTP]: Path Length (2 bytes)     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ [If HTTP]: Path (variable)           в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

WINDOW_UPDATE (0x06):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Window Size Increment (4 bytes)      в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

SETTINGS (0x03):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Setting ID (2 bytes) в”Ӯ Value (4 bytes)в”Ӯ  (repeated)
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
  Setting IDs:
    0x01 = MAX_CONCURRENT_STREAMS (default: 256)
    0x02 = INITIAL_WINDOW_SIZE (default: 65535)
    0x03 = MAX_FRAME_SIZE (default: 65535)
    0x04 = HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL (default: 30000ms)
    0x05 = COMPRESSION_ENABLED (default: 0)

ERROR (0x11):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Error Code (4 bytes)                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Message Length (2 bytes)             в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Message (variable, UTF-8)           в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
  Error codes:
    0x00000001 = PROTOCOL_ERROR
    0x00000002 = INTERNAL_ERROR
    0x00000003 = FLOW_CONTROL_ERROR
    0x00000004 = STREAM_CLOSED
    0x00000005 = FRAME_SIZE_ERROR
    0x00000006 = TUNNEL_NOT_FOUND
    0x00000007 = TIMEOUT
    0x00000008 = RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED

GOAWAY (0x12):
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Last Stream ID (4 bytes)             в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Error Code (4 bytes)                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Debug Data Length (2 bytes)          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Debug Data (variable)                в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

### 9.3 Handshake Flow

**Complete connection establishment sequence:**

```
Client                                           Server
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в•җв•җв•җ TCP SYN в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв–¶в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв•җв•җ TCP SYN-ACK в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в•җв•җв•җ TCP ACK в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв–¶в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в•җв•җв•җ TLS ClientHello в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв–¶в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     (ALPN: "drap/1")                           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв•җв•җ TLS ServerHello + Certificate в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в•җв•җв•җ TLS Finished в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв–¶ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв•җв•җ TLS Finished в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     [TLS 1.3 established, ALPN negotiated]     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ MAGIC BYTES: "DRAP" (4 bytes) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ  Protocol identification
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ VERSION: 0x0001 (2 bytes) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ  Protocol version
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв”Җв”Җ MAGIC BYTES: "DRAP" (4 bytes) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ  Server confirms
  в”Ӯ в—Җв”Җв”Җ VERSION: 0x0001 (2 bytes) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ  Agreed version
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ SETTINGS frame в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ  Client settings
  в”Ӯ     { MAX_CONCURRENT_STREAMS: 256,             в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       INITIAL_WINDOW_SIZE: 65535,              в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL: 30000 }              в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв”Җв”Җ SETTINGS frame в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ  в”Ӯ  Server settings
  в”Ӯ     { MAX_CONCURRENT_STREAMS: 256,             в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       MAX_FRAME_SIZE: 65535 }                  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ SETTINGS frame (ACK flag) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ  Acknowledge server settings
  в”Ӯ в—Җв”Җв”Җ SETTINGS frame (ACK flag) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ  в”Ӯ  Acknowledge client settings
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     [Settings negotiated]                      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ AUTH_REQ frame в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     { token: "drap_tok_abc123...",             в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       version: [1, 0],                        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       os: LINUX,                               в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       capabilities: 0b00000111 }               в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв”Җв”Җ AUTH_OK frame в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     { session_id: "550e8400-e29b-...",         в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       account: "dev@axiom.io",                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       max_tunnels: 5,                          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       max_bandwidth: 104857600 }               в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     [Authenticated, ready for tunnel requests] в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_REQ (stream 1) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     { proto: HTTP, subdomain: "myapp",         в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       inspect: true, rate_limit: 100/60 }      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ в—Җв”Җв”Җ TUNNEL_CREATED (stream 1) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     { tunnel_id: "t_xyz789",                   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       url: "https://myapp.drap.io",            в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ       subdomain: "myapp" }                     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     [TUNNEL IS LIVE]                           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     ... heartbeats every 30s ...               в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ     ... data frames flow ...                   в”Ӯ
```

**ALPN (Application-Layer Protocol Negotiation):**
The client advertises `drap/1` during TLS handshake. This allows the relay server to distinguish D-RAP client connections from regular HTTPS connections on the same IP (if needed in the future).

### 9.4 Error Handling Protocol

**Error handling philosophy:** Errors are categorized by recoverability.

```
Category 1: Stream-Level Errors (recoverable)
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
A single request/stream failed. Other streams unaffected.

Response: RST_STREAM frame on the affected stream.
Client action: Report error for that request, continue normally.

Examples:
  - Local service connection refused (localhost not running)
  - Local service timeout
  - Request too large
  
  Client вҶ’ Server:
    RST_STREAM { stream: 42, error: CONNECT_FAILED }
  
  Server action: Return 502 Bad Gateway to public client


Category 2: Tunnel-Level Errors (partially recoverable)
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
A tunnel has an issue. Other tunnels on same connection unaffected.

Response: TUNNEL_DENIED or ERROR frame with tunnel context.
Client action: Report to user, retry tunnel creation if transient.

Examples:
  - Subdomain already taken
  - Account tunnel limit reached
  - Rate limit exhausted at account level


Category 3: Connection-Level Errors (requires reconnect)
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
The entire connection is compromised.

Response: GOAWAY frame, then close TCP.
Client action: Reconnect with exponential backoff, re-establish all tunnels.

Examples:
  - Protocol error (malformed frame)
  - Version mismatch
  - Server shutting down
  - Authentication revoked
  
  Server вҶ’ Client:
    GOAWAY { last_stream: 42, error: SERVER_SHUTDOWN,
             debug: "Scheduled maintenance, back in 60s" }
  
  Client action:
    1. Stop sending new frames
    2. Wait for in-flight streams (up to last_stream) to complete
    3. Close connection
    4. Reconnect with backoff
    5. Re-send TUNNEL_REQ for all previously active tunnels


Category 4: Fatal Errors (no recovery)
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
Something fundamentally wrong.

Response: AUTH_FAIL or ERROR frame, then close.
Client action: Display error, exit.

Examples:
  - Invalid auth token
  - Account suspended
  - Banned IP
```

**Timeout hierarchy:**

```
Timeout                          в”Ӯ Duration в”Ӯ Action on Expiry
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
TCP connect timeout              в”Ӯ 10s      в”Ӯ Retry with backoff
TLS handshake timeout            в”Ӯ 10s      в”Ӯ Retry with backoff
Auth response timeout            в”Ӯ 5s       в”Ӯ Retry with backoff
Tunnel creation response timeout в”Ӯ 5s       в”Ӯ Retry once, then fail
Heartbeat response timeout       в”Ӯ 10s      в”Ӯ Mark stale, retry ping
Connection idle timeout          в”Ӯ 90s      в”Ӯ Close + reconnect (3 missed pings)
Stream idle timeout              в”Ӯ 30s      в”Ӯ RST_STREAM
Local connect timeout            в”Ӯ 5s       в”Ӯ RST_STREAM (502 to client)
Local response timeout           в”Ӯ 60s      в”Ӯ RST_STREAM (504 to client)
Graceful shutdown drain timeout  в”Ӯ 5s       в”Ӯ Force close remaining streams
```

---

---

## 10. Feature Specifications

### 10.1 HTTP Tunneling

**The primary use case.** Expose a local HTTP server via a public HTTPS URL.

```
Command:    $ drap http 3000
Result:     https://wild-fox-42.drap.io вҶ’ http://localhost:3000

Command:    $ drap http 3000 --subdomain=myapp
Result:     https://myapp.drap.io вҶ’ http://localhost:3000

Command:    $ drap http 8443 --local-https
Result:     https://abc123.drap.io вҶ’ https://localhost:8443
```

**HTTP-specific behaviors:**

1. **Host header rewriting:**
   ```
   Incoming: Host: myapp.drap.io
   Forwarded as: Host: localhost:3000
   (Configurable: --host-header=myapp.local)
   ```

2. **X-Forwarded headers injected:**
   ```
   X-Forwarded-For: 203.0.113.42       (original client IP)
   X-Forwarded-Proto: https             (original protocol)
   X-Forwarded-Host: myapp.drap.io      (original host)
   X-Drap-Tunnel-Id: t_xyz789          (tunnel identifier)
   ```

3. **WebSocket upgrade support:**
   ```
   If request has: Upgrade: websocket
   D-RAP switches stream to bidirectional byte mode
   WebSocket frames pass through unmodified
   Connection: kept alive for WebSocket duration
   ```

4. **Chunked transfer encoding:**
   ```
   If local server sends chunked response:
   D-RAP forwards chunks as they arrive (streaming)
   No buffering of entire response
   ```

5. **Error pages:**
   ```
   Local server not running:    502 Bad Gateway (branded D-RAP error page)
   Local server timeout:         504 Gateway Timeout
   Tunnel not found:             404 Not Found ("No tunnel found for this subdomain")
   Rate limited:                 429 Too Many Requests
   Auth required:                401 Unauthorized
   ```

### 10.2 TCP Tunneling

**For non-HTTP protocols:** databases, SSH, game servers, MQTT, custom protocols.

```
Command:    $ drap tcp 5432
Result:     tcp://wild-fox-42.drap.io:44301 вҶ’ tcp://localhost:5432

Command:    $ drap tcp 22 --remote-port=2222
Result:     tcp://abc123.drap.io:2222 вҶ’ tcp://localhost:22
```

**TCP-specific behaviors:**

1. **No protocol awareness:** D-RAP treats the connection as raw bytes. No parsing. No modification.

2. **One stream per connection:** Each incoming TCP connection gets its own multiplexed stream. Unlike HTTP where multiple requests share a concept, TCP connections are 1:1 with streams.

3. **Connection lifecycle tied to stream lifecycle:**
   ```
   Public client connects вҶ’ STREAM_OPEN вҶ’ CLI connects to local port
   Bytes flow bidirectionally via DATA frames
   Either side closes вҶ’ END_STREAM flag вҶ’ other side notified вҶ’ connection closed
   ```

4. **No inspection:** TCP traffic cannot be meaningfully inspected without protocol knowledge. Dashboard shows only: connection time, bytes transferred, duration, remote IP.

5. **Port allocation:**
   - Default: Random port from 40000-50000
   - `--remote-port=N`: Request specific port (subject to availability)
   - Port released immediately when tunnel closes

### 10.3 Custom Subdomains

**Allocation rules:**

```
Valid subdomain:
  - 3-63 characters
  - Lowercase alphanumeric and hyphens only
  - Cannot start or end with hyphen
  - Cannot be a reserved word
  
Reserved words (not exhaustive):
  www, api, admin, dashboard, status, mail, ftp, ssh,
  relay, control, metrics, health, drap, app, cdn,
  static, assets, media, blog, docs, support, help

Random subdomain generation:
  Format: {adjective}-{noun}-{2-digit-number}
  Examples: wild-fox-42, quiet-river-17, bright-moon-83
  
  Adjective pool: ~200 words (wild, quiet, bright, swift, calm, ...)
  Noun pool: ~200 words (fox, river, moon, tree, cloud, ...)
  Number: 10-99
  
  Total combinations: 200 Г— 200 Г— 90 = 3,600,000 unique subdomains
  Collision handling: If generated subdomain is taken, regenerate (up to 5 attempts)
```

**Subdomain lifecycle:**

```
1. Client requests subdomain "myapp"
2. Server checks routing table
3. If available:
   a. Add to routing table: "myapp" вҶ’ TunnelSession
   b. Return TUNNEL_CREATED
   c. Subdomain is now routable
4. If taken:
   a. Return TUNNEL_DENIED with SUBDOMAIN_TAKEN error
   b. Client can retry with different subdomain or request random

5. When tunnel closes:
   a. Remove from routing table
   b. Subdomain immediately available for others
   
6. Future (paid feature): Reserved subdomains that persist across sessions
```

### 10.4 Request Inspection

**Available when:** HTTP tunnels with `--inspect` flag (enabled by default).

**What is captured:**

```
Per request:
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ ID:        req_550e8400                     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Timestamp: 2024-01-15T10:30:42.123Z        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Tunnel:    myapp.drap.io                    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ REQUEST:                                     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Method:  POST                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Path:    /api/webhooks/stripe              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Headers:                                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     Content-Type: application/json           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     Stripe-Signature: t=1699999,v1=abc...   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     User-Agent: Stripe/1.0                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     X-Request-Id: req_123                    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Body (234 bytes):                          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     {                                        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ       "type": "payment_intent.succeeded",    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ       "data": {                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ         "object": {                          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ           "amount": 2000,                    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ           "currency": "usd"                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ         }                                    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ       }                                      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     }                                        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ RESPONSE:                                    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Status:  200 OK                            в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Headers:                                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     Content-Type: application/json           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Body (15 bytes):                           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ     {"received":true}                        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ TIMING:                                      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   TLS termination:    1.2ms                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Routing:            0.1ms                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Tunnel transit:     3.4ms                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Local processing:   12.8ms                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Total:              17.5ms                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ META:                                        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Remote IP:  54.187.174.169                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Replayed:   No                             в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ   Rate Limited: No                           в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

**Storage limits:**

```
In-memory ring buffer:
  - Last 500 requests per tunnel
  - Bodies up to 256KB stored inline
  - Larger bodies: stored in temp directory, referenced by path
  - Cleared when tunnel closes

SQLite persistence:
  - Last 10,000 requests total (across all tunnels)
  - Bodies up to 1MB stored as BLOBs
  - Larger bodies: filepath reference
  - Auto-pruned: DELETE WHERE timestamp < now() - interval '24 hours'

Hard limits:
  - Bodies > 10MB: not captured (only metadata recorded)
  - Binary bodies: stored as-is, displayed as hex in dashboard
  - Configurable: --inspect-body-limit=1048576
```

### 10.5 Request Replay

**Purpose:** Re-send a previously captured request to the local service. Essential for debugging webhooks.

**Replay flow:**

```
Dashboard UI:
  User finds request req_550e8400
  Clicks [Replay]
  Optional: Edit request before replay (modify headers, body)
  Clicks [Send]
  
API:
  POST /api/requests/req_550e8400/replay
  Body (optional): { "modified_headers": {...}, "modified_body": "..." }
  
Server:
  1. Load original request from storage
  2. Apply modifications if any
  3. Create a new stream on the tunnel
  4. Send STREAM_OPEN + DATA frames with request
  5. Wait for response
  6. Store as new CapturedRequest with:
     - is_replay: true
     - original_request_id: "req_550e8400"
  7. Return response to dashboard

Dashboard UI:
  Shows side-by-side:
  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ  Original         в”Ӯ  Replay          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  POST /webhook    в”Ӯ  POST /webhook   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Status: 500      в”Ӯ  Status: 200     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  12.8ms           в”Ӯ  8.2ms           в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Body: error...   в”Ӯ  Body: ok        в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

### 10.6 Tunnel Authentication

**Options available per tunnel:**

```
Option A: No Authentication (default)
  $ drap http 3000
  вҶ’ Anyone with URL can access

Option B: HTTP Basic Auth
  $ drap http 3000 --auth="username:password"
  вҶ’ Browser shows login prompt
  вҶ’ Credentials validated at relay server
  вҶ’ Not forwarded to local service

Option C: Bearer Token
  $ drap http 3000 --auth-token="my-secret-token"
  вҶ’ Requests must include: Authorization: Bearer my-secret-token
  вҶ’ OR query param: ?token=my-secret-token
  вҶ’ Token stripped before forwarding to local service

Option D: IP Whitelist
  $ drap http 3000 --allow-ip="203.0.113.0/24,198.51.100.42"
  вҶ’ Only requests from listed IPs/CIDRs allowed
  вҶ’ Others get 403 Forbidden

Option E: Combined
  $ drap http 3000 --auth="admin:pass" --allow-ip="10.0.0.0/8"
  вҶ’ Must pass BOTH auth and IP check
```

**Password hashing:**
Tunnel auth passwords are hashed with bcrypt before storage in the tunnel session. The relay server never stores plaintext passwords.

### 10.7 Rate Limiting

**Configurable via CLI:**

```
$ drap http 3000 --rate-limit=100/min
$ drap http 3000 --rate-limit=1000/hour
$ drap http 3000 --rate-limit=10/sec

Format: {count}/{window}
Windows: sec, min, hour
```

**Implementation layers:**

```
Layer 1: Per-Tunnel Rate Limit
  Configured by user (--rate-limit)
  Stored in Redis: ZSET rate:tunnel:{tunnel_id}
  Algorithm: Sliding window log
  
Layer 2: Per-Source-IP Rate Limit (automatic)
  Protects individual tunnels from single-source abuse
  Default: 60 req/min per IP per tunnel
  Stored in Redis: ZSET rate:ip:{tunnel_id}:{ip}
  
Layer 3: Global Server Rate Limit
  Protects relay server infrastructure
  Default: 50,000 req/sec total
  Implemented: In-memory atomic counter, no Redis call
  Token bucket algorithm for burst tolerance

Rate Limit Response:
  HTTP 429 Too Many Requests
  Headers:
    X-RateLimit-Limit: 100
    X-RateLimit-Remaining: 0
    X-RateLimit-Reset: 1700000060
    Retry-After: 42
  Body:
    {
      "error": "rate_limit_exceeded",
      "message": "Rate limit of 100 requests per minute exceeded",
      "retry_after_seconds": 42
    }
```

### 10.8 Active Tunnel Dashboard

**Served locally at:** `http://127.0.0.1:4040`

**Dashboard pages:**

```
PAGE 1: OVERVIEW
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

  в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ

  Shows per-tunnel:
  - Connection status, uptime, reconnection count
  - Public URL (clickable)
  - Configuration (auth, rate limit, inspect settings)
  - Request volume chart (1min, 5min, 1hr windows)
  - Status code distribution pie chart
  - Avg/p50/p95/p99 latency
  - Top paths by request count
  - Recent errors

## 11. Security Architecture

### 11.1 Threat Model

```
Threat 1: Unauthorized Tunnel Creation
  Attack:  Attacker connects to relay server, creates tunnels
  Defense: Auth tokens required, validated on every connection
  
Threat 2: Tunnel Hijacking
  Attack:  Attacker guesses subdomain of active tunnel, intercepts traffic
  Defense: Subdomains are cryptographically random or chosen by authenticated user.
           Traffic flows through authenticated tunnel connection only.
           
Threat 3: Man-in-the-Middle on Tunnel
  Attack:  Attacker intercepts traffic between client and relay
  Defense: TLS on the control connection. Certificate pinning option for CLI client.
  
Threat 4: Traffic Sniffing on Public Side
  Attack:  Intercepting HTTPS traffic to tunnel URLs
  Defense: TLS termination with valid wildcard certificate. HSTS headers.
  
Threat 5: Denial of Service
  Attack:  Flooding a tunnel with requests
  Defense: Multi-layer rate limiting (per-IP, per-tunnel, global).
           Connection limits per source IP.
  
Threat 6: Resource Exhaustion
  Attack:  Creating thousands of tunnels to exhaust server resources
  Defense: Per-account tunnel limits. Per-account bandwidth limits.
           Connection timeout enforcement.
           
Threat 7: Subdomain Squatting
  Attack:  Claiming valuable subdomains (e.g., "stripe", "github")
  Defense: Subdomains are not persistent on free tier.
           Reserved word list. Abuse reporting mechanism.

Threat 8: Local Network Scanning
  Attack:  Using D-RAP to scan the developer's local network
  Defense: CLI client ONLY connects to the explicitly specified local address/port.
           No wildcard local binding. Cannot proxy to arbitrary local addresses.
           
Threat 9: Replay Attacks on Auth
  Attack:  Capturing and replaying auth tokens
  Defense: TLS prevents capture. Tokens are long-lived but revocable.
           Future: Add token rotation, session binding.

Threat 10: Data Exfiltration via Tunnel
  Attack:  Malicious insider uses tunnel to exfiltrate data
  Defense: Outside D-RAP's scope (same as any internet connection).
           Audit logging of tunnel creation. Bandwidth monitoring.
```

### 11.2 Security Defaults

```
вң… TLS everywhere (public HTTPS + control connection)
вң… Auth tokens required (no anonymous tunnel creation)
вң… Rate limiting enabled by default
вң… Request body size limits
вң… Connection count limits per account
вң… Automatic tunnel expiry (8 hours max on free tier)
вң… No wildcard local address binding
вң… HSTS headers on all public responses
вң… X-Frame-Options: DENY on dashboard
вң… CSP headers on dashboard
вң… Secrets never logged (tokens, passwords masked in logs)
```

---

---

## 12. Concurrency Model

### 12.1 Relay Server Concurrency

**The relay server is the performance bottleneck.** It handles:
- Thousands of tunnel client connections
- Tens of thousands of public HTTP connections
- All routing, rate limiting, and inspection

**Model: async/await with tokio (Rust)**

```
