```

**Why this works for 10,000+ concurrent connections:**

- tokio tasks are ~2KB of stack (vs 8MB for OS threads)
- 10,000 tasks = ~20MB memory just for task stacks
- Work-stealing scheduler balances load across CPU cores
- `io_uring` backend on Linux for minimal syscall overhead
- No garbage collection pauses (Rust)
- Lock-free routing table (DashMap uses sharded locks, effectively lock-free for reads)

### 12.2 CLI Client Concurrency

```
tokio Runtime (client):
  Worker threads: 4 (lighter than server)
  
  Tasks:
  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ Control Connection Manager   в”Ӯ  1 task
  в”Ӯ Frame Reader                 в”Ӯ  1 task
  в”Ӯ Frame Writer                 в”Ӯ  1 task
  в”Ӯ Heartbeat Responder          в”Ӯ  1 task
  в”Ӯ Local Dashboard Server       в”Ӯ  1 task + spawned per HTTP request
  в”Ӯ Per-Stream Proxy             в”Ӯ  1 task per active request/connection
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
  
  At 100 concurrent proxied requests: ~100 tasks + 5 management tasks
  Memory: <50MB typical
```

---

---

## 13. Data Flow Diagrams

### 13.1 HTTP Request вҖ” Complete Data Flow

```
 в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ         в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ         в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
 в”Ӯ  Public   в”Ӯ  HTTPS  в”Ӯ              RELAY SERVER                    в”Ӯ  D-RAP   в”Ӯ  D-RAP    в”Ӯ   TCP    в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
 в”Ӯ  Client   в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶в”Ӯ                                              в”Ӯ  Protocolв”Ӯ  CLI      в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶в”Ӯ Local    в”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ (Browser) в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ   в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶в”Ӯ  Client   в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ App      в”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ TLS в”ӮвҶ’в”ӮRouterв”ӮвҶ’в”ӮAuthв”ӮвҶ’в”ӮRate Limitв”Ӯ   в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ :3000    в”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ           в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ  в”ӮTerm.в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ  в”ӮGateв”Ӯ  в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ   в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ           в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ          в”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ  HTTPS  в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ   в”Ӯ  D-RAP   в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ   TCP    в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ
 в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ         в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ            в”Ӯ  Protocolв”Ӯ           в”Ӯ          в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
                      в”Ӯ       в–ј                          в–ј            в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ            в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ      в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в”ӮInspector в”Ӯ            в”Ӯ Multiplexerв”Ӯ      в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ(capture) в”Ӯ            в”Ӯ(frame/send)в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ            в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ      в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ                                       в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ       в–ј                                       в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ                                в”Ӯ         в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
                      в”Ӯ  в”ӮDashboard в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ         в”ӮDashboard  в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в”ӮAPI notifyв”Ӯ                                в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ:4040      в”Ӯ
                      в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ                                в”Ӯ         в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
                      в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Data transformations at each step:

Step 1: TLS Termination
  Input:  Encrypted HTTPS bytes
  Output: Plaintext HTTP request

Step 2: Router
  Input:  HTTP request with Host header
  Output: Same request + tunnel reference

Step 3: Auth Gate
  Input:  HTTP request + tunnel auth config
  Output: Pass (continue) or Reject (401/403)

Step 4: Rate Limiter
  Input:  Request + tunnel rate config
  Output: Pass (continue) or Reject (429)

Step 5: Inspector (async, non-blocking)
  Input:  Full HTTP request
  Output: CapturedRequest stored to ring buffer + SQLite
  Note:   This does NOT block the request flow. It captures a copy.

Step 6: Multiplexer
  Input:  HTTP request bytes
  Output: D-RAP DATA frames on assigned stream ID

Step 7: Wire (relay вҶ’ client)
  Input:  D-RAP frames
  Output: Same frames, encrypted via TLS control connection

Step 8: Client Demultiplexer
  Input:  D-RAP DATA frames
  Output: HTTP request bytes for specific stream

Step 9: Local Proxy
  Input:  HTTP request bytes
  Output: TCP connection to localhost:3000, send bytes

Step 10: Local App Response (reverse flow)
  Steps 9-1 in reverse
```

### 13.2 TCP Tunnel вҖ” Complete Data Flow

```
 в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ                в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ                в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
 в”Ӯ  Public   в”Ӯ  Raw TCP       в”Ӯ    RELAY SERVER      в”Ӯ   D-RAP       в”Ӯ  D-RAP    в”Ӯ  Raw TCP    в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
 в”Ӯ  TCP      в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ  Protocol     в”Ӯ  CLI      в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶в”Ӯ Local    в”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ  Client   в”Ӯ                в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ    в”Ӯв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶в”Ӯ  Client   в”Ӯ             в”Ӯ PostgreSQLв”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ (psql)    в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ  в”ӮTCP Port Routerв”Ӯ   в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ           в”Ӯв—Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ӯ :5432    в”Ӯ
 в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ  Raw TCP       в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ:44301 вҶ’ tun#3в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ  D-RAP       в”Ӯ           в”Ӯ  Raw TCP    в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ
 в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ                в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ    в”Ӯ  Protocol     в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ             в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
                             в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ             в”Ӯ
                             в”Ӯ         в–ј             в”Ӯ
                             в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ     в”Ӯ
                             в”Ӯ  в”ӮBidirectional  в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
                             в”Ӯ  в”ӮByte Copy      в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
                             в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ(zero-copy)    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
                             в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ     в”Ӯ
                             в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Note: No TLS termination (public side is raw TCP)
      No HTTP parsing
      No inspection (just byte counters)
      No auth gate (TCP has no standard auth mechanism)
      Rate limiting: connection count only, not request-based
```

## 14. Database Schema

### 14.1 Relay Server вҖ” SQLite

```sql
-- User accounts
CREATE TABLE users (
    id              TEXT PRIMARY KEY,           -- UUID
    email           TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
    auth_token_hash TEXT NOT NULL,              -- bcrypt hash of drap_tok_...
    plan            TEXT DEFAULT 'free',        -- free, pro, enterprise
    max_tunnels     INTEGER DEFAULT 3,
    max_bandwidth   INTEGER DEFAULT 104857600,  -- 100MB/s
    created_at      TEXT NOT NULL,              -- ISO 8601
    last_seen_at    TEXT
);

-- Tunnel history (persisted after tunnel closes)
CREATE TABLE tunnel_history (
    id              TEXT PRIMARY KEY,           -- UUID
    user_id         TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES users(id),
    protocol        TEXT NOT NULL,              -- http, tcp
    subdomain       TEXT,
    local_addr      TEXT NOT NULL,              -- localhost:3000
    public_url      TEXT NOT NULL,
    started_at      TEXT NOT NULL,
    ended_at        TEXT,
    total_requests  INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
    total_bytes_in  INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
    total_bytes_out INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
    close_reason    TEXT                        -- client_disconnect, server_shutdown, timeout, error
);

CREATE INDEX idx_tunnel_history_user ON tunnel_history(user_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_tunnel_history_started ON tunnel_history(started_at);

-- Captured requests (for inspection/replay)
CREATE TABLE captured_requests (
    id                  TEXT PRIMARY KEY,       -- UUID
    tunnel_id           TEXT NOT NULL,
    timestamp           TEXT NOT NULL,
    
    -- Request
    req_method          TEXT,
    req_path            TEXT,
    req_headers         TEXT,                   -- JSON
    req_body            BLOB,                   -- Raw bytes (NULL if too large)
    req_body_path       TEXT,                   -- File path if body > 1MB
    req_body_size       INTEGER,
    req_content_type    TEXT,
    
    -- Response
    res_status_code     INTEGER,
    res_headers         TEXT,                   -- JSON
    res_body            BLOB,
    res_body_path       TEXT,
    res_body_size       INTEGER,
    res_content_type    TEXT,
    
    -- Timing
    total_duration_ms   INTEGER,
    tunnel_rtt_ms       INTEGER,
    local_duration_ms   INTEGER,
    
    -- Meta
    remote_addr         TEXT,
    is_replay           INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
    original_request_id TEXT,                   -- If replayed, points to original
    
    created_at          TEXT NOT NULL
);

CREATE INDEX idx_captured_tunnel ON captured_requests(tunnel_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_captured_timestamp ON captured_requests(created_at);

-- Auto-cleanup: delete requests older than 24 hours
-- Triggered by a background task every hour
```

### 14.2 CLI Client вҖ” SQLite (~/.drap/drap.db)

```sql
-- Local auth
CREATE TABLE config (
    key     TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    value   TEXT NOT NULL
);
-- Stores: authtoken, default_region, last_server_url

-- Request history (local copy for offline viewing)
CREATE TABLE local_requests (
    id              TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    tunnel_id       TEXT NOT NULL,
    timestamp       TEXT NOT NULL,
    method          TEXT,
    path            TEXT,
    status_code     INTEGER,
    duration_ms     INTEGER,
    req_body_size   INTEGER,
    res_body_size   INTEGER,
    created_at      TEXT NOT NULL
);

CREATE INDEX idx_local_req_tunnel ON local_requests(tunnel_id);
```

### 14.3 Redis Schema (Relay Server)

```
# Active tunnel tracking
SET active_tunnels                          вҶ’ Set of tunnel IDs
HASH tunnel:{tunnel_id}                     вҶ’ { user_id, subdomain, proto, created_at, ... }
STRING subdomain:{subdomain}                вҶ’ tunnel_id (for fast lookup)

# Rate limiting
ZSET rate:tunnel:{tunnel_id}                вҶ’ Sorted set of request timestamps
ZSET rate:ip:{tunnel_id}:{ip}              вҶ’ Sorted set per source IP per tunnel
STRING rate:global                          вҶ’ Atomic counter for global rate

# Session management
HASH session:{session_id}                   вҶ’ { user_id, connected_at, client_ip, tunnels: [...] }
EXPIRE session:{session_id} 86400           вҶ’ Auto-expire after 24h

# Metrics (real-time counters)
STRING metrics:requests:total               вҶ’ Atomic counter
STRING metrics:bytes:in                     вҶ’ Atomic counter
STRING metrics:bytes:out                    вҶ’ Atomic counter
HASH metrics:status_codes                   вҶ’ { "200": 14523, "404": 42, "500": 7 }

# Pub/Sub for multi-instance (future)
CHANNEL drap:events                         вҶ’ { type: "tunnel_created", ... }
```

## 15. API Design

### 15.1 Dashboard REST API (Go, served on :4040)

```
Base URL: http://127.0.0.1:4040/api

Authentication: None (local only, bound to 127.0.0.1)

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ
TUNNELS
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

GET /api/tunnels
  Description: List all active tunnels
  Response 200:
  {
    "tunnels": [
      {
        "id": "t_abc123",
        "protocol": "http",
        "subdomain": "myapp",
        "public_url": "https://myapp.drap.io",
        "local_addr": "localhost:3000",
        "status": "connected",
        "started_at": "2024-01-15T10:00:00Z",
        "uptime_seconds": 3600,
        "total_requests": 247,
        "total_bytes_in": 1048576,
        "total_bytes_out": 5242880,
        "config": {
          "inspect": true,
          "auth_enabled": false,
          "rate_limit": "100/min"
        }
      }
    ]
  }

GET /api/tunnels/:id
  Description: Get detailed info for a specific tunnel
  Response 200: { tunnel: { ...full details... } }
  Response 404: { "error": "tunnel_not_found" }

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ
REQUESTS
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

GET /api/requests
  Description: List captured requests
  Query params:
    tunnel_id:  Filter by tunnel (optional)
    method:     Filter by HTTP method (optional)
    status:     Filter by status code (optional)
    path:       Filter by path prefix (optional)
    limit:      Max results (default 50, max 500)
    offset:     Pagination offset
    sort:       "newest" (default) or "oldest"
  Response 200:
  {
    "requests": [
      {
        "id": "req_550e8400",
        "tunnel_id": "t_abc123",
        "timestamp": "2024-01-15T10:30:42.123Z",
        "method": "POST",
        "path": "/api/webhook",
        "status_code": 200,
        "duration_ms": 17,
        "req_body_size": 234,
        "res_body_size": 15,
        "remote_addr": "54.187.174.169",
        "is_replay": false
      }
    ],
    "total": 247,
    "has_more": true
  }

GET /api/requests/:id
  Description: Full request detail (headers, body, timing)
  Response 200:
  {
    "request": {
      "id": "req_550e8400",
      "tunnel_id": "t_abc123",
      "timestamp": "2024-01-15T10:30:42.123Z",
      "request": {
        "method": "POST",
        "path": "/api/webhook",
        "headers": {
          "Content-Type": "application/json",
          "Stripe-Signature": "t=1699...,v1=abc..."
        },
        "body": "{\"type\":\"payment_intent.succeeded\",...}",
        "body_size": 234,
        "content_type": "application/json"
      },
      "response": {
        "status_code": 200,
        "headers": {
          "Content-Type": "application/json"
        },
        "body": "{\"received\":true}",
        "body_size": 15,
        "content_type": "application/json"
      },
      "timing": {
        "tls_ms": 1.2,
        "routing_ms": 0.1,
        "tunnel_rtt_ms": 3.4,
        "local_processing_ms": 12.8,
        "total_ms": 17.5
      },
      "remote_addr": "54.187.174.169",
      "is_replay": false,
      "original_request_id": null
    }
  }

POST /api/requests/:id/replay
  Description: Replay a captured request
  Request body (optional):
  {
    "modified_headers": { "X-Custom": "value" },
    "modified_body": "...",
    "modified_path": "/api/webhook-v2"
  }
  Response 200:
  {
    "replay": {
      "original_request_id": "req_550e8400",
      "replay_request_id": "req_661f9511",
      "response": {
        "status_code": 200,
        "headers": { ... },
        "body": "...",
        "duration_ms": 14
      }
    }
  }

DELETE /api/requests
  Description: Clear all captured requests
  Query params:
    tunnel_id: Clear only for specific tunnel (optional)
  Response 204: No content

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ
METRICS
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

GET /api/metrics
  Description: Current metrics snapshot
  Response 200:
  {
    "uptime_seconds": 3600,
    "tunnels_active": 2,
    "connections_active": 14,
    "requests": {
      "total": 1247,
      "per_minute": 12.3,
      "per_second": 0.21
    },
    "bandwidth": {
      "bytes_in": 1048576,
      "bytes_out": 5242880,
      "mbps_in": 0.23,
      "mbps_out": 1.17
    },
    "status_codes": {
      "2xx": 1180,
      "3xx": 22,
      "4xx": 38,
      "5xx": 7
    },
    "latency": {
      "avg_ms": 15.2,
      "p50_ms": 12.0,
      "p95_ms": 34.0,
      "p99_ms": 89.0
    }
  }

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ
WEBSOCKET (Real-time events)
в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

WS /api/ws
  Description: Live event stream
  Events (JSON messages):
  
  { "type": "request",
    "data": { ...same as GET /api/requests/:id... } }
    вҶ’ Fired on every request through any tunnel
  
  { "type": "tunnel_connected",
    "data": { "id": "t_abc123", "url": "https://myapp.drap.io" } }
    вҶ’ Fired when a new tunnel comes online
  
  { "type": "tunnel_disconnected",
    "data": { "id": "t_abc123", "reason": "client_disconnect" } }
    вҶ’ Fired when a tunnel goes offline
  
  { "type": "metrics",
    "data": { ...same as GET /api/metrics... } }
    вҶ’ Fired every 5 seconds with updated metrics
  
  { "type": "error",
    "data": { "tunnel_id": "t_abc123", "error": "local_connect_refused" } }
    вҶ’ Fired on proxy errors
```

### 15.2 Internal Control API (between relay server components)

```
This is NOT exposed externally. It's the communication channel
between the relay server's Rust core and the Go dashboard API.

Option A: Unix Domain Socket
  The Rust server exposes a UDS at /tmp/drap-control.sock
  The Go API connects as a client
  Protocol: Simple JSON-over-newline

Option B: Shared SQLite + File-based Events  
  Both processes read/write to the same SQLite database
  Events communicated via inotify on a shared event log file

Option C: gRPC (internal)
  Rust server runs a gRPC server on localhost:4041
  Go API is a gRPC client

Chosen: Option A (Unix Domain Socket)
  Simplest, no additional dependencies, fast enough for local IPC
```

---

## 16. CLI Design

### 16.1 Command Structure

```
drap вҖ” Dynamic Relay Access Point

USAGE:
    drap <COMMAND> [OPTIONS]

COMMANDS:
    http        Start an HTTP tunnel
    tcp         Start a TCP tunnel
    start       Start tunnels from config file
    authtoken   Set or view auth token
    status      Show active tunnels
    version     Show version info
    help        Show help

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

drap http <PORT> [OPTIONS]

  Start an HTTP tunnel to local port

  ARGS:
    <PORT>                    Local port to tunnel (e.g., 3000)

  OPTIONS:
    -s, --subdomain <NAME>    Request custom subdomain
    --host-header <HOST>      Rewrite Host header (default: localhost:<PORT>)
    --local-https             Local server uses HTTPS
    --inspect                 Enable request inspection (default: true)
    --no-inspect              Disable request inspection
    --auth <USER:PASS>        Require HTTP Basic Auth on tunnel
    --auth-token <TOKEN>      Require Bearer token on tunnel
    --allow-ip <CIDRS>        Comma-separated IP/CIDR whitelist
    --rate-limit <SPEC>       Rate limit (e.g., "100/min", "10/sec")
    --bind <ADDR>             Local bind address (default: localhost)
    --region <REGION>         Relay server region (default: us-east-1)
    --log-level <LEVEL>       Log level: error, warn, info, debug, trace

  EXAMPLES:
    drap http 3000
    drap http 8080 --subdomain=myapp --auth="admin:secret"
    drap http 3000 --rate-limit=100/min --allow-ip="10.0.0.0/8"

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

drap tcp <PORT> [OPTIONS]

  Start a TCP tunnel to local port

  ARGS:
    <PORT>                    Local TCP port to tunnel (e.g., 5432)

  OPTIONS:
    --remote-port <PORT>      Request specific public port
    --allow-ip <CIDRS>        IP whitelist
    --region <REGION>         Relay server region
    --log-level <LEVEL>       Log level

  EXAMPLES:
    drap tcp 5432
    drap tcp 22 --remote-port=2222

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

drap start [OPTIONS]

  Start tunnels defined in config file

  OPTIONS:
    -c, --config <PATH>       Config file path (default: ./drap.yml)
    --log-level <LEVEL>       Log level

в•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җ

drap authtoken <TOKEN>

  Set the auth token for this machine

  ARGS:
    <TOKEN>                   Your D-RAP auth token

  The token is stored in ~/.drap/authtoken
  Obtain a token at: https://dashboard.drap.io/tokens
```

### 16.3 Config File Format (drap.yml)

```yaml
# ~/.drap/drap.yml or ./drap.yml

# Authentication
authtoken: drap_tok_abc123xyz789def456

# Global defaults
region: us-east-1
log_level: info
inspect: true

# Tunnel definitions
tunnels:
  # HTTP tunnel вҖ” frontend app
  frontend:
    proto: http
    addr: 3000
    subdomain: my-frontend
    inspect: true
    host_header: myapp.local
    
  # HTTP tunnel вҖ” API with auth and rate limiting
  api:
    proto: http
    addr: 8080
    subdomain: my-api
    inspect: true
    auth: "admin:supersecret"
    rate_limit: "100/min"
    allow_ip:
      - "10.0.0.0/8"
      - "203.0.113.42"
    
  # TCP tunnel вҖ” PostgreSQL
  database:
    proto: tcp
    addr: 5432
    remote_port: 54320
    
  # TCP tunnel вҖ” Redis
  cache:
    proto: tcp
    addr: 6379
    
  # HTTP tunnel вҖ” local HTTPS server
  secure-app:
    proto: http
    addr: 8443
    local_https: true
    subdomain: my-secure-app
    auth_token: "bearer-token-12345"
```

**Config file resolution order:**
1. CLI arguments (highest priority)
2. `./drap.yml` (project-level)
3. `~/.drap/drap.yml` (user-level)
4. Built-in defaults (lowest priority)

**Merging rules:**
- CLI args override config file
- Project config overrides user config
- `authtoken` from any source is accepted
- Tunnel definitions from config file are additive

---

---

## 17. Dashboard UI Design

### 17.1 Technology & Approach

```
Framework:     Svelte (compiled, no runtime overhead)
Styling:       Tailwind CSS (utility-first, small bundle)
Charts:        Chart.js (lightweight) or D3.js (powerful)
WebSocket:     Native browser WebSocket API
Build tool:    Vite
Bundle target: ES2020 (modern browsers)

The compiled dashboard is embedded into the Rust CLI binary.
When user runs `drap http 3000`, the local server on :4040
serves the dashboard HTML/JS/CSS from memory.

Total bundle size target: <200KB gzipped
```

### 17.2 Page Layouts

**Page 1: Overview Dashboard**

```

### 17.3 UI Component Architecture (Svelte)

```
src/
в”ңв”Җв”Җ App.svelte                    # Root component, router
в”ңв”Җв”Җ lib/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ api.js                    # REST API client
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ websocket.js              # WebSocket connection manager
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ stores/
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ tunnels.js            # Svelte store: active tunnels
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ requests.js           # Svelte store: captured requests
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ metrics.js            # Svelte store: live metrics
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ connection.js         # Svelte store: WS connection state
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ utils/
в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ format.js             # Format bytes, duration, timestamps
в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ syntax-highlight.js   # JSON/XML syntax highlighting
в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ debounce.js           # Search debouncing
в”ңв”Җв”Җ pages/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ Overview.svelte           # Main dashboard page
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ Requests.svelte           # Request inspector page
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ RequestDetail.svelte      # Single request detail + replay
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ TunnelDetail.svelte       # Single tunnel detail
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ Settings.svelte           # Configuration page
в”ңв”Җв”Җ components/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ Sidebar.svelte            # Navigation sidebar
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ StatusBadge.svelte        # Online/offline indicator
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ TunnelCard.svelte         # Tunnel summary card
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ RequestRow.svelte         # Single request in table
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ RequestExpanded.svelte    # Expanded request details
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ HeadersTable.svelte       # HTTP headers display
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ BodyViewer.svelte         # Request/response body with formatting
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ TimingBar.svelte          # Request timing waterfall
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ReplayForm.svelte         # Editable replay form
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ComparisonView.svelte     # Side-by-side original vs replay
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ LiveChart.svelte          # Real-time line chart
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ StatusCodePie.svelte      # Status code distribution
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ MetricCard.svelte         # Single metric display
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ SearchBar.svelte          # Filterable search input
в””в”Җв”Җ styles/
    в””в”Җв”Җ app.css                   # Tailwind imports + custom styles
```

## 18. Deployment Architecture

### 18.1 CLI Client Distribution

```
Distribution: Single static binary per platform

Platforms:
  - Linux x86_64    (primary)
  - Linux aarch64   (ARM servers, Raspberry Pi)
  - macOS x86_64    (Intel Macs)
  - macOS aarch64   (Apple Silicon)
  - Windows x86_64  (via MSVC or GNU toolchain)

Build: Cross-compilation using cross-rs or cargo-zigbuild

Installation methods:

  1. Direct download:
     $ curl -sSL https://install.drap.io | sh
     
  2. Homebrew (macOS/Linux):
     $ brew install drap
     
  3. Cargo:
     $ cargo install drap
     
  4. APT (Debian/Ubuntu):
     $ sudo apt install drap
     
  5. Docker (for CI environments):
     $ docker run --rm -it --net=host drap/drap http 3000
     
  6. npm (for Node.js developers):
     $ npx drap http 3000

Binary size target: <15MB (stripped, with embedded dashboard)
```

### 18.3 Docker Compose (Relay Server)

```yaml
# docker-compose.yml for relay server deployment

version: '3.8'

services:
  drap-server:
    build:
      context: ./drap-server
      dockerfile: Dockerfile
    container_name: drap-server
    restart: always
    ports:
      - "443:443"           # Public HTTPS
      - "4443:4443"         # D-RAP control
      - "40000-50000:40000-50000"  # TCP tunnels
    volumes:
      - ./certs:/etc/drap/certs:ro
      - ./data:/var/lib/drap
      - /tmp/drap-control.sock:/tmp/drap-control.sock
    environment:
      - DRAP_DOMAIN=drap.io
      - DRAP_TLS_CERT=/etc/drap/certs/fullchain.pem
      - DRAP_TLS_KEY=/etc/drap/certs/privkey.pem
      - DRAP_REDIS_URL=redis://redis:6379
      - DRAP_DB_PATH=/var/lib/drap/drap.db
      - DRAP_LOG_LEVEL=info
      - DRAP_MAX_TUNNELS_PER_USER=5
      - DRAP_MAX_CONNECTIONS=50000
      - RUST_LOG=drap_server=info
    depends_on:
      - redis
    ulimits:
      nofile:
        soft: 1000000
        hard: 1000000

  drap-dashboard:
    build:
      context: ./drap-dashboard-api
      dockerfile: Dockerfile
    container_name: drap-dashboard
    restart: always
    volumes:
      - /tmp/drap-control.sock:/tmp/drap-control.sock
      - ./data:/var/lib/drap:ro
    environment:
      - DRAP_CONTROL_SOCKET=/tmp/drap-control.sock
      - DRAP_DB_PATH=/var/lib/drap/drap.db
      - DRAP_LISTEN_ADDR=0.0.0.0:4040

  redis:
    image: redis:7-alpine
    container_name: drap-redis
    restart: always
    command: redis-server --maxmemory 512mb --maxmemory-policy allkeys-lru
    volumes:
      - redis_data:/data

  prometheus:
    image: prom/prometheus:latest
    container_name: drap-prometheus
    restart: always
    volumes:
      - ./monitoring/prometheus.yml:/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml
      - prometheus_data:/prometheus

  grafana:
    image: grafana/grafana:latest
    container_name: drap-grafana
    restart: always
    ports:
      - "3001:3000"   # Admin access only, not public
    volumes:
      - grafana_data:/var/lib/grafana
      - ./monitoring/grafana/dashboards:/etc/grafana/provisioning/dashboards
      - ./monitoring/grafana/datasources:/etc/grafana/provisioning/datasources

volumes:
  redis_data:
  prometheus_data:
  grafana_data:
```

## 19. Performance Targets & Benchmarks

### 19.1 Key Performance Indicators

```
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Metric                                        в”Ӯ Target         в”Ӯ Stretch Goal в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
в”Ӯ Added latency (relay overhead)                в”Ӯ <5ms p50       в”Ӯ <2ms p50     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Added latency (tunnel overhead)               в”Ӯ <10ms p50      в”Ӯ <5ms p50     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Concurrent tunnels per server                 в”Ӯ 5,000          в”Ӯ 50,000       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Concurrent HTTP requests per server           в”Ӯ 10,000         в”Ӯ 100,000      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Throughput per tunnel (HTTP)                   в”Ӯ 50 MB/s        в”Ӯ 200 MB/s     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Throughput per tunnel (TCP)                    в”Ӯ 100 MB/s       в”Ӯ 500 MB/s     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Tunnel establishment time                     в”Ӯ <100ms         в”Ӯ <50ms        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Client binary startup time                    в”Ӯ <500ms         в”Ӯ <200ms       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Client memory usage (idle, 1 tunnel)          в”Ӯ <30MB          в”Ӯ <15MB        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Client memory usage (active, 100 req/s)       в”Ӯ <100MB         в”Ӯ <50MB        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Server memory usage (1000 tunnels, idle)      в”Ӯ <500MB         в”Ӯ <200MB       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Server CPU usage (1000 req/s total)           в”Ӯ <25% (8 core)  в”Ӯ <10%         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Dashboard load time                           в”Ӯ <1s            в”Ӯ <500ms       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Dashboard bundle size (gzipped)               в”Ӯ <200KB         в”Ӯ <100KB       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Request inspection overhead                   в”Ӯ <1ms           в”Ӯ <0.5ms       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Rate limiting check overhead                  в”Ӯ <0.5ms         в”Ӯ <0.1ms       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Reconnection time after disconnect            в”Ӯ <3s            в”Ӯ <1s          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ Zero-downtime server restart                  в”Ӯ Supported      в”Ӯ вҖ”            в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

### 19.2 Benchmark Suite

```
Benchmark 1: Raw Tunnel Throughput
  Tool: iperf3 through D-RAP TCP tunnel
  Measure: MB/s in both directions
  Compare: Direct connection vs D-RAP tunnel
  Target: <10% throughput reduction

Benchmark 2: HTTP Request Latency
  Tool: wrk2 (constant throughput load generator)
  Setup: wrk2 вҶ’ D-RAP tunnel вҶ’ simple HTTP server (return 200 OK)
  Measure: p50, p95, p99, p99.9 latency
  Load levels: 100, 500, 1000, 5000, 10000 req/s
  Target: p99 <20ms at 1000 req/s

Benchmark 3: Concurrent Tunnels
  Tool: Custom script that creates N tunnels
  Measure: Memory usage, CPU usage, tunnel creation time
  Levels: 100, 500, 1000, 5000, 10000 tunnels
  Target: 5000 tunnels in <2GB memory

Benchmark 4: Connection Storm
  Tool: Custom script that creates 10000 TCP connections simultaneously
  Measure: Accept rate, time to establish all, error rate
  Target: 0% error rate, <5s to accept all 10000

Benchmark 5: Long-Running Stability
  Tool: 24-hour stress test with varying load
  Measure: Memory leaks, latency degradation, connection failures
  Target: No memory growth, stable latency, 0 unrecoverable failures

Benchmark 6: Dashboard Performance
  Tool: Lighthouse, custom WebSocket stress test
  Measure: Load time, FPS with 100 req/s streaming, memory usage
  Target: 60 FPS, <300MB browser memory after 1 hour
```

### 19.3 Optimization Strategies

```
Strategy 1: Zero-Copy I/O
  Where: Relay server TCP proxy, data frame forwarding
  How: Use bytes::Bytes (reference-counted byte buffers)
       Avoid copying request/response bodies
       Use splice() / sendfile() syscalls where possible
  Impact: Major throughput improvement for large payloads

Strategy 2: io_uring (Linux)
  Where: Relay server socket I/O
  How: tokio-uring or io-uring crate for async I/O
       Reduces syscall overhead by batching
  Impact: 10-30% latency reduction at high concurrency

Strategy 3: Object Pooling
  Where: Frame parsing, byte buffer allocation
  How: Pre-allocate frame buffers, reuse after processing
       slab allocator for stream state objects
  Impact: Reduces allocation pressure, fewer GC-like pauses (even in Rust, allocator contention matters)

Strategy 4: Lock-Free Data Structures
  Where: Routing table, metrics counters, connection registry
  How: DashMap (sharded locks), AtomicU64, crossbeam-epoch
  Impact: Eliminates contention on hot paths

Strategy 5: Connection Reuse
  Where: Client вҶ’ local server, Redis connections
  How: Connection pooling with keep-alive
  Impact: Eliminates TCP handshake per request

Strategy 6: Efficient Serialization
  Where: Wire protocol frame parsing
  How: Zero-copy deserialization (parse header in-place, reference payload slice)
       No intermediate allocations for frame routing
  Impact: <1Ојs per frame parse

Strategy 7: Batch Operations
  Where: Request inspection storage, metrics updates
  How: Buffer captured requests, flush to SQLite in batches (every 100ms)
       Aggregate metrics in memory, flush counters periodically
  Impact: Reduces I/O operations by 10-100x
```

## 20. Testing Strategy

### 20.1 Test Pyramid

```
                    в•ұв•І
                   в•ұ  в•І
                  в•ұ E2E в•І           ~20 tests
                 в•ұ Tests  в•І         Playwright + custom scripts
                в•ұв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв•І
               в•ұ            в•І
              в•ұ Integration   в•І      ~100 tests
             в•ұ Tests           в•І     Real TCP connections, real tunnels
            в•ұв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв•І
           в•ұ                     в•І
          в•ұ   Unit Tests           в•І   ~500 tests
         в•ұ                          в•І  Pure logic, no I/O
        в•ұв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв•І
```

### 20.2 Unit Tests (Rust + Go)

```
drap-protocol/
  - Frame serialization/deserialization for ALL frame types
  - Frame header parsing edge cases (max length, zero length, invalid type)
  - Stream state machine transitions (valid and invalid)
  - Flow control window calculations
  - Random subdomain generation (uniqueness, format validation)
  
drap-client/
  - Config file parsing (valid, invalid, partial)
  - Config merging (CLI args + file + defaults)
  - Auth token validation format
  - Reconnection backoff calculation
  - Request capture formatting
  
drap-server/
  - Subdomain routing (exact match, not found, reserved words)
  - Rate limiting algorithm (allow, deny, window sliding, burst)
  - Auth validation (Basic Auth parsing, token matching, bcrypt verify)
  - IP whitelist matching (IPv4, IPv6, CIDR ranges)
  - Tunnel allocation (port assignment, subdomain collision handling)
  - HTTP parser (methods, headers, chunked encoding, keep-alive)
  
drap-dashboard-api/
  - API endpoint handlers (request/response format)
  - Query parameter parsing and validation
  - Metrics aggregation logic
```

### 20.3 Integration Tests

```
Test Category 1: Tunnel Lifecycle
  - Client connects вҶ’ authenticates вҶ’ creates tunnel вҶ’ closes вҶ’ disconnects
  - Client creates multiple tunnels simultaneously
  - Client with invalid token вҶ’ rejected
  - Client requests taken subdomain вҶ’ denied, retries with random
  - Server shutdown вҶ’ client reconnects вҶ’ tunnels re-established
  
Test Category 2: HTTP Proxying
  - Simple GET request through tunnel вҶ’ 200 response
  - POST with JSON body вҶ’ correctly forwarded and returned
  - Large response body (10MB) вҶ’ streamed correctly
  - Chunked transfer encoding вҶ’ handled correctly
  - Request with many headers (50+) вҶ’ all forwarded
  - WebSocket upgrade вҶ’ persistent bidirectional communication
  - Concurrent requests (100 simultaneous) вҶ’ all succeed
  - Local server not running вҶ’ 502 Bad Gateway
  - Local server slow (10s) вҶ’ eventually responds (before 60s timeout)
  - Local server unreachable after initial connection вҶ’ appropriate error
  
Test Category 3: TCP Proxying
  - PostgreSQL connection through tunnel вҶ’ query succeeds
  - SSH connection through tunnel вҶ’ interactive session works
  - Large data transfer (1GB) through TCP tunnel вҶ’ completes without corruption
  - Binary data (random bytes) вҶ’ bit-perfect transfer
  - Multiple simultaneous TCP connections вҶ’ all independent
  - TCP connection close from either side вҶ’ clean teardown
  
Test Category 4: Authentication
  - Tunnel with Basic Auth вҶ’ unauthenticated request вҶ’ 401
  - Tunnel with Basic Auth вҶ’ correct credentials вҶ’ proxied
  - Tunnel with Bearer Token вҶ’ correct token вҶ’ proxied
  - Tunnel with Bearer Token вҶ’ wrong token вҶ’ 403
  - Tunnel with IP whitelist вҶ’ allowed IP вҶ’ proxied
  - Tunnel with IP whitelist вҶ’ blocked IP вҶ’ 403
  
Test Category 5: Rate Limiting
  - Send requests at rate below limit вҶ’ all succeed
  - Send requests at rate above limit вҶ’ excess rejected with 429
  - Wait for window to expire вҶ’ requests succeed again
  - Rate limit headers present in all responses
  - Per-IP rate limiting independent between IPs
  
Test Category 6: Request Inspection
  - Request captured with correct method, path, headers, body
  - Response captured with correct status, headers, body
  - Timing breakdown is reasonable (>0ms, <total)
  - Request replay sends identical request вҶ’ response captured
  - Modified replay sends modified request вҶ’ response captured
  - Ring buffer overflow вҶ’ oldest requests evicted
  - Large body (>1MB) вҶ’ stored to file, referenced correctly
  
Test Category 7: Connection Resilience
  - Network interruption (iptables drop) вҶ’ client reconnects
  - Slow network (tc netem delay) вҶ’ tunnel works with higher latency
  - Packet loss (tc netem loss 5%) вҶ’ tunnel works with retransmissions
  - Server restart вҶ’ client reconnects, tunnels re-established
  - Client restart вҶ’ clean tunnel teardown on server
  
Test Category 8: Concurrency & Stress
  - 100 tunnels from 100 clients simultaneously
  - 1000 concurrent HTTP requests through single tunnel
  - Sustained 10,000 req/s for 60 seconds вҶ’ no errors
  - Memory usage under load вҶ’ no unbounded growth
  - CPU usage under load вҶ’ reasonable (not 100%)
```

### 20.4 End-to-End Tests

```
E2E Test 1: Developer Workflow
  1. Start local Express server on :3000
  2. Run `drap http 3000 --subdomain=test-e2e`
  3. Wait for "online" status
  4. curl https://test-e2e.drap.io вҶ’ verify response matches local
  5. Open dashboard at :4040 вҶ’ verify request appears
  6. Click replay вҶ’ verify replayed request appears
  7. Ctrl+C drap вҶ’ verify tunnel closes
  8. curl https://test-e2e.drap.io вҶ’ verify 404 tunnel not found

E2E Test 2: Webhook Simulation
  1. Start local webhook handler on :8080
  2. Run `drap http 8080 --inspect`
  3. Send simulated Stripe webhook POST
```
  4. Verify webhook received by local handler
  5. Verify request captured in dashboard
  6. Verify Stripe-Signature header present
  7. Modify handler to return 500
  8. Replay webhook from dashboard
  9. Verify 500 response captured
  10. Fix handler to return 200
  11. Replay again вҶ’ verify 200

E2E Test 3: TCP Database Tunnel
  1. Start PostgreSQL on :5432
  2. Run `drap tcp 5432`
  3. Note assigned public port
  4. Connect psql to public address
  5. CREATE TABLE, INSERT, SELECT вҶ’ verify data integrity
  6. Close psql вҶ’ verify stream closes cleanly
  7. Reconnect вҶ’ verify new stream works

E2E Test 4: Multi-Tunnel Config File
  1. Create drap.yml with 3 tunnels (2 HTTP, 1 TCP)
  2. Start local services on all 3 ports
  3. Run `drap start --config drap.yml`
  4. Verify all 3 tunnels online
  5. Send traffic to each вҶ’ verify correct routing
  6. Stop one local service вҶ’ verify others unaffected
  7. Restart stopped service вҶ’ verify requests work again

E2E Test 5: Auth & Rate Limiting
  1. Run `drap http 3000 --auth="user:pass" --rate-limit=5/min`
  2. curl without auth вҶ’ 401
  3. curl with wrong auth вҶ’ 403
  4. curl with correct auth вҶ’ 200
  5. Send 5 requests rapidly вҶ’ all succeed
  6. Send 6th request вҶ’ 429 with Retry-After header
  7. Wait for window reset вҶ’ next request succeeds

E2E Test 6: Dashboard Real-Time Updates
  1. Start tunnel with inspect
  2. Open dashboard in Playwright browser
  3. Send HTTP request to tunnel
  4. Verify request appears in dashboard within 1 second (no page refresh)
  5. Send 10 requests rapidly
  6. Verify all 10 appear in order
  7. Verify live chart updates
  8. Verify metrics counters increment

E2E Test 7: Reconnection
  1. Start tunnel
  2. Send traffic вҶ’ verify working
  3. Kill relay server process
  4. Verify client shows "reconnecting" status
  5. Restart relay server
  6. Verify client reconnects automatically
  7. Verify same subdomain is reclaimed
  8. Send traffic вҶ’ verify working again
  9. Total downtime < 5 seconds
```

### 20.5 Chaos Testing

```
Chaos Test 1: Network Partition
  Tool: tc (traffic control) / iptables
  Scenario: Drop all packets between client and server for 30s
  Expected: Client detects disconnect, reconnects after partition heals
  Verify: All in-flight requests get error responses (not hung forever)
          Tunnel re-establishes within 5s of partition healing

Chaos Test 2: Memory Pressure
  Tool: stress-ng --vm 4 --vm-bytes 90%
  Scenario: Consume 90% of server memory
  Expected: Server remains responsive (might be slower)
            OOM killer does not kill drap-server
            Graceful rejection of new tunnels if memory critically low

Chaos Test 3: CPU Starvation
  Tool: stress-ng --cpu 8
  Scenario: Consume all CPU cores
  Expected: Latency increases but no dropped connections
            Heartbeats still sent (tokio scheduler is fair)
            Requests eventually complete (increased timeout tolerance)

Chaos Test 4: Disk Full
  Tool: dd if=/dev/zero of=/tmp/fill bs=1M
  Scenario: Fill disk where SQLite database lives
  Expected: Request inspection gracefully degrades (stops capturing)
            Tunnel proxying continues unaffected (doesn't require disk)
            Error logged, alert raised

Chaos Test 5: Redis Down
  Tool: docker stop drap-redis
  Scenario: Redis becomes unavailable
  Expected: Rate limiting falls back to in-memory (less accurate)
            Session tracking degrades gracefully
            Tunnels continue to function
            Automatic reconnection to Redis when it recovers

Chaos Test 6: Slow Client
  Tool: Custom client that reads tunnel data at 1 byte/s
  Scenario: Client cannot keep up with incoming traffic
  Expected: Flow control kicks in (WINDOW_UPDATE not sent)
            Server buffers up to limit, then back-pressures public clients
            Public clients get 503 or delayed responses
            Other tunnels on same server are unaffected

Chaos Test 7: Malicious Frames
  Tool: Custom script sending garbage D-RAP frames
  Scenario: Invalid frame types, oversized payloads, invalid stream IDs
  Expected: Server rejects each invalid frame with appropriate error
            Connection closed with GOAWAY if protocol violation is severe
            Server does not crash, panic, or leak memory
            Other clients completely unaffected
```

## 21. Development Phases & Timeline

### Phase 0: Foundation (Week 1-2)

```
Goal: Project setup, protocol library, basic TCP communication

Tasks:
  в–Ў Repository structure (Cargo workspace for Rust, Go module, Svelte project)
  в–Ў CI/CD pipeline (GitHub Actions: build, test, lint for all components)
  в–Ў D-RAP wire protocol library (drap-protocol crate)
    в–Ў Frame struct definitions
    в–Ў Frame serializer (struct вҶ’ bytes)
    в–Ў Frame deserializer (bytes вҶ’ struct)
    в–Ў Frame type constants and flags
    в–Ў Unit tests for all frame types (round-trip serialization)
  в–Ў Basic TCP server that accepts connections
  в–Ў Basic TCP client that connects
  в–Ў Send/receive frames over TCP
  в–Ў Integration test: client connects, sends AUTH_REQ, server responds AUTH_OK

Deliverable: Two binaries that can connect and exchange D-RAP protocol frames.
```

### Phase 1: Basic HTTP Tunnel (Week 3-5)

```
Goal: The core product вҖ” tunnel an HTTP request from public URL to localhost

Tasks:
  в–Ў TLS integration (rustls) on both control and public connections
  в–Ў Wildcard certificate loading
  в–Ў Stream multiplexing implementation
    в–Ў Stream ID assignment
    в–Ў Stream state machine
    в–Ў Concurrent stream handling
  в–Ў Subdomain routing
    в–Ў Host header parsing
    в–Ў Routing table (DashMap)
    в–Ў Random subdomain generation
  в–Ў HTTP request parsing (from raw bytes)
    в–Ў Request line parsing
    в–Ў Header parsing
    в–Ў Body reading (Content-Length and chunked)
  в–Ў HTTP response construction
    в–Ў Status line, headers, body
    в–Ў Error pages (502, 504, 404)
  в–Ў Tunnel lifecycle
    в–Ў TUNNEL_REQ вҶ’ TUNNEL_CREATED flow
    в–Ў TUNNEL_CLOSE вҶ’ TUNNEL_CLOSED_ACK flow
    в–Ў Clean teardown of all streams on tunnel close
  в–Ў Client-side local proxy
    в–Ў Connect to localhost
    в–Ў Forward request bytes
    в–Ў Read response bytes
    в–Ў Return via tunnel
  в–Ў CLI interface (clap)
    в–Ў `drap http <PORT>` command
    в–Ў `--subdomain` option
    в–Ў Terminal output with URL display
  в–Ў Heartbeat mechanism (PING/PONG)
  в–Ў Integration tests: full HTTP request lifecycle

Deliverable: `drap http 3000` gives you a public URL that works.
             This is the MVP. Everything after this is features.
```

### Phase 2: TCP Tunnel + Connection Resilience (Week 6-7)

```
Goal: TCP tunneling support and robust connection handling

Tasks:
  в–Ў TCP tunnel implementation
    в–Ў TCP port allocator (40000-50000 range)
    в–Ў TCP listener per allocated port
    в–Ў Bidirectional byte copy (public вҶ” tunnel вҶ” local)
    в–Ў Stream lifecycle for TCP (connection-scoped)
    в–Ў `drap tcp <PORT>` CLI command
  в–Ў Connection resilience
    в–Ў Auto-reconnection with exponential backoff + jitter
    в–Ў Tunnel re-establishment after reconnect
    в–Ў Graceful handling of network interruptions
    в–Ў Connection state machine (CONNECTING вҶ’ CONNECTED вҶ’ RECONNECTING вҶ’ ...)
  в–Ў Flow control
    в–Ў WINDOW_UPDATE frame handling
    в–Ў Per-stream window tracking
    в–Ў Back-pressure propagation
  в–Ў SETTINGS frame exchange during handshake
  в–Ў GOAWAY frame for graceful shutdown
  в–Ў Integration tests: TCP tunnel, reconnection scenarios

Deliverable: TCP tunneling works. Tunnels survive brief network interruptions.
```

### Phase 3: Security Features (Week 8-9)

```
Goal: Authentication, rate limiting, and access control on tunnels

Tasks:
  в–Ў Client authentication
    в–Ў Auth token generation (server-side)
    в–Ў Token storage (~/.drap/authtoken)
    в–Ў AUTH_REQ/AUTH_OK/AUTH_FAIL flow
    в–Ў `drap authtoken <TOKEN>` command
  в–Ў Tunnel authentication
    в–Ў HTTP Basic Auth (--auth="user:pass")
      в–Ў WWW-Authenticate response
      в–Ў Authorization header parsing
      в–Ў Credential validation (bcrypt)
    в–Ў Bearer token (--auth-token="TOKEN")
      в–Ў Authorization: Bearer header parsing
      в–Ў ?token= query parameter fallback
    в–Ў Header stripping (don't forward auth headers to local service)
  в–Ў IP whitelisting
    в–Ў CIDR parsing and matching
    в–Ў IPv4 and IPv6 support
    в–Ў --allow-ip CLI option
  в–Ў Rate limiting
    в–Ў Redis integration
    в–Ў Sliding window algorithm
    в–Ў Per-tunnel rate limiting
    в–Ў Per-IP rate limiting
    в–Ў Rate limit response headers
    в–Ў 429 response with Retry-After
    в–Ў --rate-limit CLI option
  в–Ў X-Forwarded headers injection
  в–Ў HSTS headers on all responses
  в–Ў Security-related unit and integration tests

Deliverable: Tunnels can be locked down with auth, rate limiting, and IP restrictions.
```

### Phase 4: Request Inspection & Replay (Week 10-12)

```
Goal: Full request/response capture, dashboard API, and replay

Tasks:
  в–Ў Request capture system
    в–Ў Capture request (method, path, headers, body)
    в–Ў Capture response (status, headers, body)
    в–Ў Timing breakdown (TLS, routing, tunnel RTT, local processing)
    в–Ў In-memory ring buffer (last 500 per tunnel)
    в–Ў SQLite persistence (last 24 hours)
    в–Ў Large body handling (file storage for >1MB)
    в–Ў Binary body detection and handling
  в–Ў Dashboard REST API (Go)
    в–Ў GET /api/tunnels
    в–Ў GET /api/tunnels/:id
    в–Ў GET /api/requests (with filtering, pagination)
    в–Ў GET /api/requests/:id (full detail)
    в–Ў POST /api/requests/:id/replay
    в–Ў DELETE /api/requests
    в–Ў GET /api/metrics
  в–Ў Dashboard WebSocket API
    в–Ў WS /api/ws
    в–Ў Real-time request events
    в–Ў Tunnel status events
    в–Ў Metrics update events (every 5s)
  в–Ў Internal communication (Rust server вҶ” Go API via Unix Domain Socket)
  в–Ў Replay engine
    в–Ў Load original request from storage
    в–Ў Apply modifications
    в–Ў Send through tunnel as new stream
    в–Ў Capture replay response
    в–Ў Link replay to original request
  в–Ў --inspect / --no-inspect CLI options
  в–Ў Integration tests: capture, storage, retrieval, replay

Deliverable: Full request inspection and replay working via API.
             Ready for the dashboard UI to consume.
```

### Phase 5: Dashboard UI (Week 13-15)

```
Goal: Beautiful, real-time web dashboard

Tasks:
  в–Ў Svelte project setup with Vite and Tailwind
  в–Ў WebSocket connection manager (auto-reconnect)
  в–Ў Svelte stores for reactive state management
  в–Ў Overview page
    в–Ў Metric cards (tunnels, requests, latency, errors)
    в–Ў Live request rate chart (Chart.js)
    в–Ў Active tunnel list
    в–Ў Status code distribution
    в–Ў Bandwidth display
  в–Ў Request inspector page
    в–Ў Filterable request table
    в–Ў Real-time updates (new rows appear at top)
    в–Ў Expandable request detail
    в–Ў Headers display (formatted table)
    в–Ў Body viewer (JSON syntax highlighting, XML formatting, hex for binary)
    в–Ў Timing waterfall bar
    в–Ў "Copy as cURL" button
    в–Ў "Export as JSON" button
  в–Ў Replay page
    в–Ў Pre-populated form from original request
    в–Ў Editable method, path, headers, body
    в–Ў Send button
    в–Ў Side-by-side comparison view
  в–Ў Tunnel detail page
    в–Ў Status, uptime, URL
    в–Ў Config display
    в–Ў Per-tunnel request chart
    в–Ў Per-tunnel metrics
  в–Ў Settings page
    в–Ў Current configuration display
    в–Ў Connection info
  в–Ў Embed compiled dashboard into Rust binary
  в–Ў Local HTTP server on :4040 serves dashboard
  в–Ў E2E tests with Playwright

Deliverable: Full dashboard accessible at http://127.0.0.1:4040
```

### Phase 6: Config File & Multi-Tunnel (Week 16-17)

```
Goal: Config file support, multiple simultaneous tunnels

Tasks:
  в–Ў YAML config file parser (drap.yml)
  в–Ў Config file resolution (project вҶ’ user вҶ’ defaults)
  в–Ў Config merging with CLI arguments
  в–Ў `drap start --config drap.yml` command
  в–Ў Multiple tunnel management
    в–Ў Multiple TUNNEL_REQ over single control connection
    в–Ў Terminal display showing all tunnel URLs
    в–Ў Dashboard showing all tunnels
  в–Ў Per-tunnel configuration (different auth, rate limits per tunnel)
  в–Ў Graceful multi-tunnel shutdown
  в–Ў Integration tests: config file parsing, multi-tunnel operation

Deliverable: Define multiple tunnels in a config file, start them all with one command.
```

### Phase 7: Polish & Production Readiness (Week 18-20)

```
Goal: Performance optimization, documentation, distribution

Tasks:
  в–Ў Performance optimization
    в–Ў Benchmarks (wrk2, iperf3, custom load tools)
    в–Ў Profile with perf / flamegraph
    в–Ў Optimize hot paths based on profiling results
    в–Ў Zero-copy I/O implementation
    в–Ў Connection pool tuning
  в–Ў Binary distribution
    в–Ў Cross-compilation for all platforms
    в–Ў GitHub Releases with pre-built binaries
    в–Ў Install script (curl | sh)
    в–Ў Homebrew formula
    в–Ў Docker image for relay server
  в–Ў Documentation
    в–Ў README with quick start
    в–Ў Architecture document (this document, refined)
    в–Ў CLI reference (auto-generated from clap)
    в–Ў API reference
    в–Ў Protocol specification
    в–Ў Deployment guide
    в–Ў Contributing guide
  в–Ў Monitoring
    в–Ў Prometheus metrics endpoint on relay server
    в–Ў Grafana dashboard templates
    в–Ў Health check endpoint
  в–Ў Logging
    в–Ў Structured logging (JSON format)
    в–Ў Log levels properly used
    в–Ў Sensitive data redaction
  в–Ў Error messages
    в–Ў User-friendly error messages for all failure modes
    в–Ў Actionable suggestions ("Is your auth token correct?")
    в–Ў Debug mode with verbose output
  в–Ў Chaos testing suite (as defined in Section 20.5)
  в–Ў Load testing (sustained stress for 24 hours)
  в–Ў Security audit (manual review of all auth/crypto code)

Deliverable: Production-ready, distributable, documented tunnel platform.
```

в”ӮTOTAL   в”Ӯ в–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳв–Ҳ (20 weeks)      в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

MVP (usable product): Week 5 (basic HTTP tunnel)
Feature-complete:     Week 17 (all features implemented)
Production-ready:     Week 20 (optimized, tested, documented)

## 23. Risk Assessment & Mitigation

```
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ Risk                        в”Ӯ Level   в”Ӯ Mitigation                               в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

в”Ӯ features, never finish      в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ is usable alone. Ship incrementally.     в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ stream state machine is     в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ machine. Fuzzing frame parser. Reference в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ complex, easy to get wrong  в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ HTTP/2 implementations for correctness.  в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ Performance not meeting     в”Ӯ MEDIUM  в”Ӯ Benchmark early (Phase 1). Profile with  в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ                             в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ allocations. Consider io_uring.          в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ async Rust is hard,         в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ lib). Read tokio docs thoroughly. Don't  в”Ӯ

в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

в”Ӯ input                       в”Ӯ         в”Ӯ Fuzzing with cargo-fuzz. Manual security в”Ӯ

в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
в”Ӯ DNS/Certificate setup вҖ”     в”Ӯ LOW     в”Ӯ Document setup clearly. Provide helper   в”Ӯ

```

### Contingency Plans

```
If behind schedule by >2 weeks:
  вҶ’ Cut request replay feature (P1 becomes P2)
  вҶ’ Cut config file support (use CLI only)
  вҶ’ Ship dashboard with read-only inspection (no replay)
  вҶ’ Skip Windows support initially

If multiplexing proves too complex:
  вҶ’ Fall back to one-connection-per-stream model
  вҶ’ Less efficient but much simpler
  вҶ’ Optimize later once basic flow works

If Rust async is too painful:
  вҶ’ Port to Go (second choice language)
  вҶ’ Sacrifice some performance for development speed
  вҶ’ Still proves the same networking concepts

If performance targets aren't met:
  вҶ’ Profile and fix obvious bottlenecks first
  вҶ’ Lower targets to "good enough" (e.g., <10ms instead of <5ms)
  вҶ’ Document what would need to change for better performance
  вҶ’ This is a portfolio project, not a production SaaS

If Go dashboard API adds too much complexity:
  вҶ’ Write dashboard API in Rust (same binary as relay server)
  вҶ’ Use warp or axum for the REST + WebSocket server
  вҶ’ Eliminates IPC entirely
  вҶ’ Single binary for entire relay server + dashboard
```

---

---

## 24. Future Roadmap

### Version 1.1 вҖ” Enhanced Protocol Support

```
в–Ў HTTP/2 tunnel support
  - HPACK header compression
  - Server push passthrough
  - Full HTTP/2 multiplexing within tunnel stream

в–Ў gRPC tunneling
  - HTTP/2 based, should work with HTTP/2 support
  - Bidirectional streaming
  - Protobuf-aware inspection (decode messages in dashboard)

в–Ў WebSocket-first tunneling
  - Option to use WebSocket as transport instead of raw TCP
  - Works through corporate proxies that block non-HTTP traffic
  - `drap http 3000 --transport=ws`
```

### Version 1.2 вҖ” Multi-Region & Scalability

```
в–Ў Multi-region relay servers
  - us-east, eu-west, ap-south
  - GeoDNS routes to nearest region
  - `drap http 3000 --region=eu-west-1`

в–Ў Relay server clustering
  - Redis Cluster for shared state
  - Consistent hashing for tunnel assignment
  - Cross-region tunnel migration on failover

в–Ў Horizontal scaling
  - Multiple relay server instances behind L4 load balancer
  - Sticky sessions based on tunnel ID
  - Shared routing table via Redis
```

### Version 1.3 вҖ” Developer Experience

```
в–Ў Plugin system
  - Custom request/response transformers
  - Pre-built plugins: CORS headers, response delay, mock responses
  - Plugin written in WASM for safety and portability

в–Ў Team features
  - Shared tunnels visible to team members
  - Persistent subdomains for teams
  - Audit logging

в–Ў IDE integrations
  - VS Code extension: start/stop tunnels from editor
  - JetBrains plugin
  - Dashboard embedded in IDE panel
```

### Version 1.4 вҖ” Advanced Networking

```
в–Ў UDP tunneling
  - DNS server exposure
  - Game server tunneling
  - VoIP/WebRTC relay

в–Ў QUIC transport
  - Replace TCP tunnel transport with QUIC
  - Eliminates head-of-line blocking
  - Better performance on lossy networks
  - 0-RTT connection establishment

в–Ў P2P mode
  - Direct peer-to-peer tunnel (no relay server)
  - STUN/TURN for NAT traversal
  - Relay as fallback only
  - Lower latency, no bandwidth limits
```

### Version 2.0 вҖ” Platform

```
в–Ў D-RAP Cloud (hosted service)
  - Free tier: 1 tunnel, 100 req/min, random subdomain
  - Pro tier: 10 tunnels, unlimited requests, custom subdomains
  - Enterprise: self-hosted relay server + management UI

в–Ў API & Integrations
  - REST API for programmatic tunnel management
  - Terraform provider
  - GitHub Actions integration
  - Slack notifications for tunnel events

в–Ў Analytics
  - Request analytics per tunnel
  - Error rate monitoring
  - Latency percentile tracking
  - Usage-based billing
```

---

## 25. Why This Project Matters

### 25.1 For Hiring Managers

```
What a normal fresher builds:
  "I used Express.js to make a REST API that talks to MongoDB"

What this project demonstrates:
  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ                                                                   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ Custom TCP/IP networking from raw sockets                     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ Binary protocol design (own wire format)                      в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ TLS termination and certificate management                   в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ  вң“ NAT traversal and reverse tunneling                          в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ  вң“ Rate limiting algorithms (sliding window, token bucket)       в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ  вң“ CLI tool design with excellent DX                            в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ Multi-language project (Rust + Go + Svelte)                  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ Systems programming (zero-copy I/O, memory efficiency)       в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ Database design (SQLite schema, Redis data modeling)          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ DevOps (Docker, systemd, kernel tuning, monitoring)          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  вң“ Security engineering (threat modeling, defense in depth)      в”Ӯ

### 25.2 Skills Proven by Each Component

```
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

### 25.3 What Sets This Apart

```
1. IT'S A REAL PRODUCT
   Not a tutorial project. Not a TODO app. Not a CRUD API.
   This is a tool that developers actually use every day.
   ngrok has 5 million+ users. This is that, built from scratch.

2. IT'S NETWORKING, NOT CRUD
   99% of portfolio projects are "React frontend talks to Express backend
   talks to MongoDB." This project operates at the TCP/IP level.
   It proves understanding that most developers never achieve.

3. IT'S SYSTEMS PROGRAMMING
   Custom binary protocol. Zero-copy I/O. Connection multiplexing.
   This is the kind of work that powers the infrastructure
   everyone else builds on top of.

4. IT COMBINES BREADTH AND DEPTH
   Protocol design + CLI tooling + web dashboard + deployment.
   Low-level networking + high-level UX. Rust + Go + Svelte.
   Proves versatility without sacrificing depth.

5. IT HAS MEASURABLE QUALITY
   Not "I built it and it works." 
   It has benchmark targets. It has chaos tests. It has a threat model.
   It proves engineering maturity, not just coding ability.

6. THE DOCUMENTATION PROVES THE THINKING
   This document itself demonstrates:
   - System design ability
   - Technical decision-making with clear rationale
   - Understanding of tradeoffs
   - Long-term thinking (roadmap, scalability)
   - Attention to detail
   - Communication skills

   Most freshers can't explain WHY they made technical decisions.
   This document explains every single one.
```

### 25.4 The One-Line Resume Entry

```
D-RAP вҖ” Built a full tunneling platform (like ngrok) from scratch:
custom binary protocol, TCP/TLS proxy, connection multiplexing,
NAT traversal, subdomain routing, rate limiting, request inspection
& replay, real-time dashboard. Rust + Go + Svelte. 20K+ LOC.
Handles 10K+ concurrent connections with <5ms proxy overhead.
```
